Current Commentary

U.S. Neutrality and International Sanctions

— Star

Now that Geneva has determined to impose sanctions against Italy, outside the League of Nations system are the three major countries of the United States, Japan, and Germany. Among these three countries, the United States is the most noteworthy. During the Great War of 1914, the United States, in its capacity as a neutral country, strongly advocated freedom of the seas, leading to severe clashes with the British Navy. Had it not been for Germany's submarine policy, a decisive battle between Britain and the United States might have been unavoidable. Having learned this lesson, the London authorities must consider the attitude of the United States in any international sanctions, as the United States has the power to break through the international sanctions net, both in trade and in military force, thus rendering Geneva's actions ineffective. However, in recent years, Americans have also awakened to the folly of their actions during the European War. Driven by merchants seeking profit and bankers seeking investment, the United States was drawn into an unnecessary war. Although the war initially brought economic prosperity, the post-war recession soon engulfed the United States. To this day, millions of unemployed people still suffer from the aftereffects of the European War. Therefore, there are many who advocate never getting involved in another world war and voluntarily relinquishing some maritime freedom and neutral rights. The Neutrality Act passed by Congress a few months ago and the recent ban on arms exports to belligerent countries are based on this desire and awareness.

What we should pay attention to now is whether, under this Neutrality Act, when the League of Nations implements sanctions against Italy, the neutral United States will have the opportunity to clash with the League of Nations member states. According to news from Pi Yue, former U.S. Secretary of State Stimson wrote to the New York Times, saying that the U.S. ban on arms exports is not enough to prevent the United States from being drawn into the vortex of crisis. The sale of American cotton and other goods to Italy will soon cause serious conflicts between the United States and League member states. Therefore, Stimson advocated expanding cooperation between the United States and the League of Nations to stop the Italian-Ethiopian War. The incompatibility of neutralism and sanctionism is a clear principle of international law. Sanctions use the power of a group to stop and punish a member of the group for illegal acts. Neutral parties, regardless of the group's opinion, do not take a position on right or wrong of each member, who is correct and who is mistaken, and only watch from the sidelines, without taking a hostile or friendly stance towards any party. Therefore, the ban on arms must apply to both Italy and Ethiopia, without limiting trade only against Italy. President Roosevelt's proclaimed ban is narrow in scope, and cotton, copper, and iron, which can be used by Italy to manufacture weapons, are not prohibited from export. However, importing these items into Abyssinia would be impossible for the backward black nation to turn into weapons. This is neutrality that is not neutral. The Neutrality Act passed this year does not prohibit lending and extending credit to belligerent countries, while the League of Nations' financial sanctions plan includes this item. Allowing American bankers to take such an unscrupulous risk means that America's financial power can greatly increase Italy's fighting power, while it is of no benefit to Abyssinia. This is also neutrality that is not neutral. All of these can cause conflict between Geneva and Washington, and the so-called conflict between Geneva and Washington is tantamount to a conflict between Britain and the United States, as only these two countries have large navies on the Atlantic Ocean. However, whether the United States will undermine international sanctions depends entirely on the scope and duration of this war. If the war is short-term and local, the United States will not want to re-enter the mistakes of 1917 for the sake of profit. If not, enticed by Italy and the great development of overseas markets during the war, filled with surplus capital and surplus production, and with unemployed workers and farmers, the United States will not be able to resist the lure of profit and the loss of overseas trade caused by international sanctions, and will come into conflict with Britain. A spark can start a prairie fire, and American public opinion, driven by emotions, may also be drawn into a major war due to the infringement of neutral rights.

Beijing Municipal Government Urges Jiangpu County and Pukou to Demarcate Boundaries

Hubei Gypsum Salt Tax is Under the Jurisdiction of the Ministry

(Nanjing) The gypsum salt produced in Yingcheng, Tianmen, and Gong'an counties in Hubei Province was previously taxed by the Provincial Department of Finance. The Ministry of Finance unified the national salt administration and brought it under the jurisdiction of the Ministry. After negotiations with the Hubei Provincial Government and the Department of Finance, Zhang Fengwu, an auditor of the Salt Affairs Office, was appointed as the Director of the Gypsum Salt Tax Bureau to take over. The gypsum salt tax rate in the province is only 20 cents per dan, while the official salt is 10 yuan per dan. Therefore, in the past, the official salt in the province lost more than 4 million yuan per year due to the popularity of gypsum salt sales. Now that the gypsum salt is under the jurisdiction of the Ministry, it will start to increase the tax rate. The funds from the gypsum salt tax that the Provincial Department of Finance should receive each year will still be allocated by the Central Accounting Office. (14th dispatch)

Stopping the East African War - The League of Nations Encounters Another Touchstone - Delaying Sanction Actions Damages Authority - If It Fails Again, Disaster is Imminent

(London) Representatives of the member states of the League of Nations General Assembly are actively implementing severe economic sanctions against Italy today. Although it is publicly stated here that Geneva's agile development over the past few weeks aims to promote peace, optimists cannot but worry about the difficulty of the League of Nations' actions and the lack of consensus on sanctions, which may delay its implementation and thus fail to stop the East African war. If so, it is generally believed that the authority of the League of Nations will suffer a fatal blow. World peace advocate Cecil declared today that if the League of Nations fails due to lack of perseverance, disaster will soon break out. If its efforts to stop the war can indeed restore peace and uphold justice, a new era of international issues will see the dawn. (14th dispatch from Guomin)

International Financial Sanctions Against Italy - Cutting off All Public and Private Political Dealings - Approved by the Committee of Eighteen Nations in Charge

(Geneva) Today, the Committee of Eighteen of the League of Nations met to discuss economic sanctions against Italy and passed a resolution proposed by the Financial Subcommittee to prohibit all financial dealings with the Italian government and Italian civilians. At 6 pm tonight, the Sanctions Coordination Committee will hold a plenary meeting to discuss how to make the resolution effective immediately. (14th dispatch from Reuters)

(Geneva) The Committee of Eighteen Nations held a meeting at 10:30 this morning and passed the financial sanctions measures formulated by the Financial Subcommittee yesterday. It also discussed economic sanctions. According to our correspondent, Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov explained the proposal put forward by his country's representative Potemkin the day before, namely, those countries that refuse to implement Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant should be restricted financially and economically. He also asked the League of Nations to pay attention to the serious difficulties caused by the opposition of Hungary, Australia, and Albania, saying that if a certain country refuses to cooperate with the League of Nations, the entire plan currently being drafted by the League of Nations will inevitably encounter obstacles. The Soviet government's proposal the day before was intended to prevent this. In addition, the chairman of the Committee of Eighteen Nations presented a report outlining the committee's discussions and said that appropriate measures have been taken to keep the contents of the meeting confidential. The representatives of the participating countries were very moved by the chairman's remarks. (14th dispatch from Havas)

(Geneva) The Financial Subcommittee organized by the Committee of Eighteen Nations held a closed-door meeting from 4:15 pm and lasted for a long time. It drafted the following financial sanctions measures to be submitted to the Committee of Eighteen Nations for review tomorrow:

(1) Immediately prohibit lending to the Italian government. All public bonds issued by or on behalf of the Italian government, whether issued in or outside the country, are prohibited from being purchased by public or private entities.

(2) Prohibit lending to the Italian government through bank loans or other loans. Any loan contracts, even those signed previously, are prohibited from being fulfilled. (3) Prohibit lending to Italian government agencies or private individuals or companies within Italy. (4) Prohibit the purchase of stocks issued by individuals or companies within Italy.

(5) Prohibit lending to individuals or companies within Italy through bank loans or other loans. Contracts concluded with individuals or companies within Italy, which are currently valid, are also prohibited from being fulfilled. (6) Those who have concluded contracts with individuals or companies within Italy to issue bonds or stocks must prohibit the continued issuance of the unissued portion. (7) Governments of all countries should consult with each other to prohibit the above-mentioned business, whether handled directly by Italy or through persons of any other nationality.

The Committee of Eighteen Nations is scheduled to meet tomorrow morning and will generally approve the above suggestions. It will continue to study purely economic sanctions measures, namely, (1) prohibiting the flow of raw materials to Italy, and (2) prohibiting or restricting trade with Italy. (13th dispatch from Havas)

(Geneva) According to a communiqué issued by the Secretariat of the League of Nations, the Committee of Eighteen Nations held a meeting and the chairman, the Portuguese Foreign Minister, passed two proposals: (1) fully publish the news to facilitate journalists and prevent false news, and (2) pass the sanctions measures drafted by the Financial Subcommittee and slightly revise the original plan. The contents are (a) prohibiting direct or indirect lending of funds to Italy, (b) prohibiting bank loans or other loans, and (c) prohibiting the issuance of bonds on behalf of the Italian government and public institutions or private enterprises within the country. Once this measure is notified to all member states, the governments of each country will notify the Committee of Eighteen Nations of the implementation arrangements. When the Committee of Eighteen Nations discussed the sanctions measures, representatives of several member states requested explanations on the following items: first, whether Italian companies' branches in foreign countries and foreign companies' branches in Italy should be prohibited from remitting funds; second, whether the sanctions measures apply to Italian insurance companies; and third, whether funds allocated by various countries to the Italian Red Cross, which are of a charitable nature, are also prohibited. (14th dispatch from Havas)

League of Nations Asks Member States to Provide Reports - Britain Cancels Arms Ban to Ethiopia

(Geneva) The Coordination Committee on Sanctions of the General Assembly of the League of Nations, which passed the recommendation made by the Sixteen Nations Subcommittee on the 11th of this month to ban arms exports to Italy, has notified all member states. The Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, has sent a special telegram to each country, requesting them to report to the League of Nations as soon as possible any useful information, i.e. to provide a list of the laws, orders, and regulations promulgated for the implementation of this recommendation. (14th dispatch from Havas)

(London) The ban on arms exports to Ethiopia has been lifted. If British arms dealers transport arms to Ethiopia and apply for export passports, the Ministry of Commerce will consider them. (14th dispatch from Reuters)

Britain and the Netherlands Advocate Cutting off Diplomatic Relations with Italy - Some Countries Disagree

(Geneva) It is heard that British Minister Without Portfolio Eden is scheduled to return to London in the middle of next week to report to the British government on the resolutions adopted by the League of Nations for the implementation of Article 16 of the Covenant. The British delegation hopes that economic and financial sanctions will be implemented within three days. It is also heard that the British mainland, its autonomous territories, and the Dutch delegation all agree to cut off diplomatic relations with Italy, but the governments of some other countries have expressed their opposition, believing that negotiations for a peaceful settlement are still possible. Cutting off diplomatic relations would close the door to negotiations with Italy. (13th dispatch from Havas)

Austria Opposes Sanctions - Saying It Will Lead to War

(Vienna) Austrian Foreign Minister Weidege spoke at the flag-granting ceremony for the home guard in Gofrasch, Styria, today, opposing the implementation of sanctions against Italy, saying, "We should be loyal to the League of Nations, but we should also be loyal to our allies. Adopting sanctions will actually lead to the danger of war." (13th dispatch from Havas)

Tense Anglo-Italian Relations - Italy Accuses Britain of Inciting - The Mediterranean Trap Incites Suspicion

(Rome) A government spokesperson today accused Britain of inciting a tense Anglo-Italian situation, leading to fears of a European war. According to the Min Sheng Bao, Britain is now determined to expand the war to defeat fascist Italy. The concentration of the British Navy in the Mediterranean only incites suspicion. Who believes Eden's claim that the British do not want to provoke Italy? According to the naval authorities, British warships have not returned salutes to Italian ships since October 7, which can be said to disregard international etiquette. This kind of provocative and infringing behavior makes Italy have to be on guard. (14th dispatch from Guomin)

Hague dispatch - Britain has added two cannons to the sea defense of Agger, and the seriousness of the League of Nations' preparations to implement sanctions against Italy has also increased. (13th dispatch from Guomin)

Ethiopian Religious Holy Land - Aksum is Occupied by Italian Troops - Bloodless Battle Line Extends Sixty Miles - The Southern Route Targets Harar for Attack

Addis Ababa - Aksum, the religious center of Ethiopia, was occupied by Italian troops today. Historically, the kings of Ethiopia were enthroned in this city. (13th dispatch from Guomin)

Addis Ababa - After the Italian troops occupied Aksum, the northern battle line now extends 60 miles, and can advance unimpeded. What remains is only geographical disadvantage. The well-equipped troops will go straight to Magal along the camel road. (14th dispatch from Guomin)

(Rome) News from the front line here says that Italian troops have occupied the city of Aksum without bloodshed. Although this news has not been officially confirmed, it comes from reliable sources. Yesterday, the Coptic Church of Egypt surrendered to the Italian troops, and the Italian troops, in view of the fact that this city is a holy place for religion in Ethiopia and has many ancient monasteries and churches, did not fire any cannons. (14th dispatch from Havas)

Addis Ababa - Thousands of Ethiopian soldiers are now passing through Jijiga to the Ogaden front in southeastern Ethiopia. There are only small battles there now, but it is expected that Italian troops will launch a large-scale attack sooner or later. At the same time, the mobilization near Harar is almost complete. This place is the target of the Italian army's attack from Somalia. It is heard that the monthly salaries of Ethiopian soldiers are now doubled than usual. By the end of the week, there will be no major battles. The Italian army has built a road to Addis Ababa, which is considered a remarkable achievement. General Taibono, Commander-in-Chief of the Italian Army in East Africa, officially received Aschwa on this new road yesterday. The Italian army is preparing to continue its attack on the one hand, and is engaged in propaganda among the tribes of Ethiopia on the other hand. Ethiopians all know the danger of Italy's "golden propaganda," because it is rumored in Addis Ababa that seven Somali leaders were found by the Italian army to have a large number of Italian coins hidden and were shot as spies. The Italian side has spread the news of Ethiopian troops fleeing and surrendering to the Italian army, while it is also rumored in Addis Ababa that the Somali leader Samatari has led 2,000 people to surrender to the Ethiopian army. It is also said that Somali soldiers are now fleeing from the Italian army every day. Harar is the location of the main camp of the southern Ethiopian army, and the arrangements for defending the skies against attack have been greatly strengthened. Many anti-aircraft guns are placed on small surrounding hills that are not easily detected. The Ethiopian authorities have denied the claim that the Italian vanguard has reached a certain location only 60 miles from Harar. (11th dispatch from Reuters)

Italian Troops Arriving in File after File

Port of Messina, Italy - The steamship "Doskana" carrying 120 officers and 1,800 soldiers from the 19th Infantry Division, machine gun teams, and many military police officers, set sail from here at 8 pm and sailed to the Italian port of Massawa in East Africa. (14th dispatch from Havas)

Facing Each Other from Afar - Another Puppet Show Will Appear - An Ethiopian General Who Surrendered Claims to Be a Direct Descendant of the Dynasty - Looks Very Much Like a Black Porter in the U.S. Railway Bureau

(Rome) Some people predict that Prime Minister Mussolini will ennoble the Ethiopian General Gebre Krestos, who surrendered, as Emperor of Ethiopia. According to Gebre Krestos, who claims to be a direct descendant of the Ethiopian dynasty, he fled from the Ethiopian army's position yesterday with his troops and surrendered to General Taibono, Commander of the Italian Army. As soon as the Italian army occupies the city of Aksum, the new Emperor Gebre Krestos will declare his enthronement and coronation in the city and accept Italian protection. (13th dispatch from Havas)

Asmara - Chief Gebre Krestos, who surrendered to the Italian army a few days ago and may become the puppet emperor of northern Ethiopia, arrived here today. An Associated Press reporter encountered him in a barber shop and saw him buying three large bottles of perfume and several spray bottles, seemingly intending to give them as gifts to his Malak species mistress. Foreign observers all said that Gebre Krestos can be said to have come here to enjoy Italian civilization. Gebre is about 27 years old, wearing a beautiful yellow military uniform with red stripes on the side seams of his trousers. At first glance, he looks very much like a black porter in a U.S. railway sleeping car. (13th dispatch from Guomin)

Small Contact in the South - Italian Planes Constantly Reconnoitering

Addis Ababa - According to news from the Ogaden region here, the troops led by General Nasibo, Commander-in-Chief of the Ethiopian Southern Army, have made contact with the subordinates of General Graziano of the Italian Army, but there has been no major battle. The Ethiopian infantry seems to be advancing along the border of British Somaliland, with aircraft providing cover. Many planes are now conducting reconnaissance flights. If they encounter a large Ethiopian army, they will immediately drop bombs. As for the Ethiopian army, it is temporarily taking a wait-and-see attitude and does not intend to open fire until the Italian army reaches the mountains in front of Harar. (12th dispatch from Havas)

Italy Notifies Ethiopian Government - No Bombing of Railway Lines - Result of Application by Envoys from Various Countries

Addis Ababa - This agency's special dispatch, the Italian government has notified that it will not drop bombs on the railway from Djibouti to the Ethiopian capital, but only on the condition that Ethiopia does not use the railway to transport military supplies. It is heard that the Ethiopian government replied, expressing its agreement. (13th dispatch from Havas)

(London) The British, American, Belgian, French, German, and Egyptian, and Greek Envoys in Addis Ababa drafted a resolution, which British Ambassador Sir Drummond telegraphed to the Italian government today, asking them to note that the cities of Addis Ababa and Diredawa on the railway from Addis Ababa to Djibouti are not fortified and have many foreigners living there. Foreign Minister Su Wei Zhi replied that he would pay attention to this fact and notify the military authorities. It is expected that other countries will also make the same statement to the Italian government. (14th dispatch from Reuters)

Rome Intelligence: A Thousand Abyssinian Soldiers Surrender to Italy

(Rome) A report has just been received here from Adigrat, Abyssinia, stating that a thousand armed Abyssinians approached the Italian soldiers' garrison outside Magal city on the afternoon of Saturday. They surrendered to the Italian army. These Abyssinians came from the eastern part of Tigre Province. They possessed new-style rifles from the Belgian Herstal factory and fifty swift horses, equipped with fragmentation grenades. They claimed to be willing to fight against the current Abyssinian Emperor, Haile Selassie, because of their opposition to the Tigrean dynasty's descendant, Ras Gugsa, who had previously surrendered to the Italian army. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

Italian Flags Hung Throughout Adowa, General De Bono Enters the City

(Rome) According to the Roman newspaper "Il Popolo di Roma," General De Bono, the High Commissioner of Italian East Africa, has arrived in Adowa. He departed from Asmara in Italian Eritrea on Saturday evening, stayed overnight in Adi Ugri, and arrived outside Adowa city on Sunday morning. Citizens lined the streets to welcome him for a stretch of 160 kilometers. The palace in the city, where the former Abyssinian Emperor Tewodros II resided, was covered in Italian flags. Machine guns were positioned in front of the palace for defense. When De Bono entered the city, the band played the royal march and the Fascist youth anthem. General Maravigna, who led the capture of Adowa, led local dignitaries in welcoming him. De Bono then delivered a short speech and reviewed the troops. Finally, a memorial unveiling ceremony was held for the Italian soldiers who died in 1896 and 1935. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

British Preparedness, Air Force Sufficient to Cope

Zeila, British Somaliland. An Associated Press reporter, passing through the desert behind this place today, learned that the authorities of British Somaliland are already prepared for any surprises in the Italian-Abyssinian conflict. This place is a vital town. Although the dwellings inside are only mud huts, there is also a state-of-the-art airfield. If the war in the southwest develops, aerial operations here can proceed with ample resources. The authorities here deny that the camel route from Zeila to Jijiga has been closed due to the fighting in Harar, and they also deny that Japanese merchants are using camel caravans to smuggle arms into Abyssinia. The local governor, Barry, is the only white man among the 5,000 black residents here. (National News Agency dispatch, 13th)

British Embassy in Addis Ababa Urges Nationals to Leave

Addis Ababa. The British Embassy here today warned British women, children, and other British nationals who are currently able to leave Abyssinia to depart as soon as possible and not delay any longer. There are about 100 British citizens, 200 British Indians, 100 Arabs, 50 Anamites, and about 50 Scandinavians and Portuguese under British protection in Addis Ababa. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

Italian Envoy Has Not Left Addis Ababa, Effectively Under House Arrest, Rail Traffic Unobstructed

Addis Ababa. Count Vinci, the Italian envoy, has still not left here. It is said that he is ill and his condition is quite worrying. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

Addis Ababa. After repeatedly refusing to leave the country, Italian Minister Count Vinci has now been placed under house arrest by the Abyssinian government. The same is true for Lieutenant Colonel Gadolini, the military attaché of that country. Diplomats from various countries, including the French Minister, have been unable to meet with Vinci as they wished. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

Addis Ababa. Italian Minister Vinci has agreed to depart together next Wednesday after the arrival of the Italian consular staff from Magalo. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

Djibouti, French Somaliland. According to a special dispatch from this agency, all the staff of the Italian Legation in Abyssinia, except for Minister Count Vinci and Military Attaché Lieutenant Colonel Gadolini, arrived here yesterday afternoon from Addis Ababa. European, Arab, and Indian residents of Abyssinia are still leaving Abyssinia in droves. Each train coming from Addis Ababa carries many foreigners. The railway from Addis Ababa to Djibouti is still operating normally. The treaty regarding the railway stipulates that the trains should operate as usual unless it is physically impossible. The railway company authorities have taken various appropriate measures in the technical field to maintain traffic even if the tracks are cut or bombed by aircraft. The company has prepared locomotives, rails, and various materials to meet urgent needs. In addition, troops are stationed near important stations and bridges for protection. Furthermore, according to the staff of the Afar station on the railway, Abyssinian soldiers did shoot down an Italian aircraft on October 11, killing one pilot and two soldiers on board. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

Yemen Reinforces Red Sea Defenses, Muslims Quite Indignant About Italian Actions

(London) According to a correspondent for the Daily Telegraph in Aden, the King of Yemen is now reinforcing the defenses of the key points on the Red Sea coast, especially focusing on locations such as Jizan, Qahzah, and Hodeidah. As the sick soldiers of the Italian East African Expeditionary Force recently intended to be sent to Yemen for recuperation, the King of Yemen has refused. In order to prevent any contingencies, he has decided to take the above-mentioned measures. Furthermore, the people of the Arabian Peninsula are very indignant about Italy's aggression against Abyssinia. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

Italian Prime Minister Sends Representative to England, Carrying Important Mission, Purpose of Trip is to Gauge Public Opinion, So That Future Negotiations Have a Basis

(London) According to a dispatch to the Daily Telegraph from a correspondent in Rome, General Ricciotti Garibaldi, leader of the Italian veterans' organization and friend of Prime Minister Mussolini (i.e., the grandson of the Italian patriot Giuseppe Garibaldi), will arrive here from Rome tomorrow. Garibaldi's arrival is ostensibly for private affairs, but according to the Daily Telegraph's speculation, Garibaldi may be here on an unofficial mission from Mussolini to gauge public opinion so that there is a basis for discussing and resolving the Italian-Abyssinian dispute in the future. After he arrives in England, he will undoubtedly explain the Italian view to British liberals and other members of Parliament. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

Anti-Italian Demonstrations in London, Paris, and South Africa, Paper Images of Mussolini Burned

(London) Today, demonstrations were held in Paris and Cape Town to protest against Italy's war against Abyssinia, and a similar demonstration was held in Hyde Park in London. Speakers mostly condemned Mussolini's actions as an unforgivable act of imperialist aggression. In Paris, one hundred people were arrested by the authorities for demonstrating, but all except six, who were detained for minor offenses, were released. Special guards were stationed in front of the Italian embassy to prevent accidents, but the demonstrators only moved along the main streets and did not disturb the Italian embassy. In Cape Town today, more than a thousand people participated in the demonstration, and a large paper image of Mussolini was burned in public. Police were also guarding the Italian embassy in London, but there were no demonstrations in front of the embassy. (Reuters dispatch, 13th)

Aloisi Addresses American Public Via Radio Broadcast, Defends Italian Policy

(Geneva) Italian representative Aloisi recently delivered a radio broadcast here to the American people, explaining Italy's view of the Italian-Abyssinian conflict, counting the following items: (1) The League of Nations has treated Italy unfairly; (2) Italy does not recognize Abyssinia as a unified country. Abyssinia can actually be divided into the area directly under the central government and the vassal part, whose subjects are subjected to various inhumane rule; (3) When Italy voted in 1922 to approve Abyssinia's accession to the League of Nations, this situation in Abyssinia already existed, but at that time, Abyssinia's accession to the League of Nations had various conditions attached, which have not been fulfilled since then; (4) Italy's actions do not violate the Kellogg-Briand Pact, as the Kellogg-Briand Pact allows countries to fight for self-defense, and in the past ten years, there have been as many as ninety incidents on the border between Abyssinia and Italian colonies; (5) Italy's interests in Abyssinia are related to Italy's survival, which has been repeatedly recognized by treaties signed in 1891, 1894, 1906, and 1925; (6) The League of Nations has adopted a double standard regarding the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, which is tantamount to creating a cocoon to trap itself. Aloisi's conclusion is that to achieve a peaceful solution, it is necessary for (1) the League of Nations to abandon its double standard, and (2) the League of Nations Covenant should be harmonized with current needs. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

Canadian Diplomatic Policy Becomes Election Material for All Parties, Striving to Avoid Being Drawn into the East African War Vortex, Commercial War Against Japan Will Be Intensified

Ottawa. Canada's diplomatic relations are quite important for tomorrow's election. Diplomatic policy has become campaign material for all parties today. The attitude towards the commercial war against Japan and the East African war has become a matter of discussion. Regarding the Japanese issue, Prime Minister Bennett firmly declared that the Japanese government's imposition of a 50% tariff on Canadian exports aims to force the Canadian government to abandon its adjustment plan. However, the Canadian government believes that changing its policy is tantamount to opening Canada's market and making it vulnerable to foreign aggression. Bennett also said that the Liberal leader's criticism of the government's tariff policy cannot help but encourage Japan's attitude. Regarding the Italian-Abyssinian war, the Canadian government is striving to avoid getting involved. Bennett declared that the Canadian government does not want to get involved in a war that has nothing to do with Canada's interests. However, this statement has conditions attached, namely that if Canada's interests are affected, the government may freely participate in any war with the approval of Parliament. Canada has little interest in this issue between Italy and Abyssinia, but if the war spreads to Europe, it will naturally affect Canada's rights. Liberal leader King and Reconstruction Party leader Stevens both insisted that Canada should not be drawn into the vortex, and should not interfere in foreign affairs without the approval of Parliament. (National News Agency dispatch, 13th)

Incident of Japanese-Puppet Troops Crossing the Border, Soviet Union Protests to Japan, Border Conflicts Constantly Occurring, Puppet Foreign Ministry Files Counter-Protest

(Tokyo) Russian Ambassador Yurenev personally met with Foreign Minister Hirota this morning and protested about the Manchukuo soldiers firing at Soviet Russian guards three times north of Wuzhan, especially focusing on the incident on October 12 when a Manchukuo sentinel squad swept a detachment of Russian border guards with machine guns. At that time, the Russian soldiers also returned fire. The ambassador did not specify the number of casualties. The "Manchukuo" authorities claimed that it was because the Russian soldiers crossed into the Manchukuo border that they opened fire to drive them back into Russian territory. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

(Tokyo) Soviet Russian Ambassador Yurenev visited Foreign Minister Hirota at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 10:30 this morning and lodged a protest in writing regarding the new disputes that occurred on October 8 and 12. Moreover, regarding the new disputes that occurred twice in the Suifen River area, he lodged a serious protest based on the Russian investigation, stating that the incidents occurred due to the invasion of the border by the Manchukuo security forces, and proposed that in order to clarify the responsibility for the disputes, a border committee should be organized between Russia, Japan, and "Manchukuo" in accordance with the Russian proposal. Foreign Minister Hirota replied that he only learned about the conflict between the Russian and Manchukuo soldiers after reading the newspaper, but the truth is unknown, so he must consult with "Manchukuo" before he can understand the facts. He also said that the Russian committee proposal will be forwarded to Manchukuo to solicit opinions before a reply can be given. In addition, the disputes occurred due to the uncertainty of the border line, so he insisted that it is necessary to determine the border line in order to resolve the issue. The Russian ambassador also considered this for a long time before leaving at noon. (Denstu dispatch, 14th) The "Manchukuo" Ministry of Foreign Affairs instructed the Harbin Special Envoy to protest to the Soviet Consul General on the 14th, conveying the government's message, due to the fact that Soviet border guards crossed the eastern border, resulting in incidents. (Japan United Press dispatch, 14th)

(Moscow) The antagonism between Japan and Russia seems to be increasing today. Yesterday, the Soviet Russian government formally announced the conflict between the soldiers of the two countries on the Songhua River. According to the report of the headquarters of the Soviet Russian Far East Army in Khabarovsk, fifty Japanese-Manchukuo soldiers crossed the river in the Grodekovo area on Saturday, using smoke screens as cover, and repelled twenty Russian guards with rifles and machine guns. The Ministry of the Army has studied this telegram today, and the report also stated that both sides suffered casualties. There have been conflicts before. Yurenev, the Soviet Russian ambassador to Japan, has been ordered to protest to Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota, and it is expected that he will personally visit Foreign Minister Hirota on Monday. It is reported that the Russian envoy will construct a mixed committee to determine the responsibility for the conflicts that have occurred over the past few months. Both the Soviet Russian Foreign Ministry and the Japanese Embassy issued statements today, claiming that there is no danger of war. However, Soviet Russian officials privately expressed concern that the Japanese Kwantung Army may disregard the government and act arbitrarily, hoping to take advantage of the world's eventful autumn to expand its territory in northern Asia. The Soviet Russian side believes that the Japanese army has long had the ambition to occupy the coastal provinces of Siberia, and the Japanese military has always called this area "a sharp arrow directly aimed at the heart of Japan." The statement issued by the Soviet Russian government today is roughly as follows: (National News Agency dispatch, 13th)

The Truth of the Incident, Russia and Japan Have Different Views

On the 6th of this month, in the Grodekovo area, a Soviet border patrol (including two mounted guards) was attacked by Manchukuo troops who invaded Soviet territory three kilometers from the border. The Manchukuo troops, numbering about twenty, were commanded by a Japanese officer. They opened fire on the Soviet mounted guards.

On the 8th of this month, about fifty Japanese-Manchukuo troops were found in the same location in Soviet territory. The Soviet government strongly protested to the Japanese-Manchukuo governments for the invasion of Soviet territory by the Japanese-Manchukuo troops. Unexpectedly, on

The 12th of this month, at 4:05 p.m. (Khabarovsk time), about fifty troops again invaded Soviet territory near the location where the incidents occurred on the 6th and 8th. They advanced about one kilometer into Soviet territory and opened fire on the Soviet patrol (including two mounted guards). Another two teams of Soviet patrols, with eighteen soldiers, were about two and a half kilometers away from the Japanese-Manchukuo troops and immediately rushed to rescue the first patrol team. The Japanese-Manchukuo troops fired rifles and machine guns at the Soviet patrol teams. In order to facilitate their advance, they set fire to dry grass. They took advantage of the smoke to advance towards the Soviet patrol teams. As a result of the firing, several Soviet border guards were killed or wounded, and the same was true for the Japanese-Manchukuo side.

After receiving the news of this border intrusion, the Soviet government immediately instructed its ambassador to Japan to lodge a strong protest, and at the same time suggested establishing a mixed committee to investigate the truth of the matter. (TASS dispatch, Moscow, 13th)

(Changchun) The Kwantung Army released the following details of the conflict between the Russian and Manchukuo troops on the afternoon of the 14th:

On October 6, a conflict occurred between Soviet and Manchukuo troops. On October 12 at 3:00 p.m., the army dispatched an investigation team consisting of Sergeant Major Nemoto of the Kenpeitai (military police) and two Manchukuo officers related to the conflict to investigate the truth on the ground, and "dispatched the Manchukuo" Border Surveillance Team of thirty-two people to escort them. When the group was establishing a marker at the location of the incident twenty kilometers north of the Suifen River, suddenly fifty Russian soldiers began firing with five heavy machine guns, but did not issue any warning to the investigation team beforehand. The Japanese-Manchukuo investigation team had no choice but to fight back. In this battle, one Japanese military police officer, one leader, and four Manchukuo soldiers were killed. Five more Manchukuo soldiers were injured. The director of the Suifen River Special Agency has dispatched Captain Nakamura of the garrison unit to the site to conduct an investigation. (Japan United Press dispatch, 14th)

(Moscow) Regarding the border conflict between the Soviet Union and Manchukuo, the Soviet Foreign Ministry notified the Japanese Embassy in the Soviet Union on the 13th that the nature of this matter cannot be the cause of a war between Japan and the Soviet Union. Also, the Japanese Embassy authorities pointed out the errors made by the Soviet Union, saying that although there are reports of Japanese and Manchukuo troops attacking the Soviet patrol, the Japanese government has denied it. (Denstu dispatch, 13th)

Kwantung Army Indignant, Conferring on Countermeasures

(Harbin) The circumstances of the recent conflict on the Russian-Manchukuo border released by the Japanese side are quite different from those described by the Soviet Russian side. All sectors of the Japanese community here believe that the Soviet Russian authorities are deliberately trying to create a serious incident, and they expect that if such incidents occur again in the future, they will deal with them with severe action. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

(Changchun) The Kwantung Army held a meeting of its top leaders this morning to discuss countermeasures. As for the root cause of the dispute, it is due to the uncertainty of the border line and the lack of sincerity of Soviet Russia. Therefore, a decisive attitude will be adopted towards the incident. (Denstu dispatch, 14th)

To Prevent Japanese-Puppet Troops from Invading Territorial Waters, Red Army Concentrates in Khabarovsk, 200,000 Ground Troops, 1,000 Warplanes, More Cruisers and Submarines Deployed to Far East

(Harbin) After the Japanese-puppet troops invaded Russian territory, the Soviet military authorities, in view of the fact that the Japanese-puppet navy will invade Soviet territorial waters, have greatly increased their alert. Recently, more than twenty cruisers and submarines have been transferred to the vicinity of Khabarovsk. On the ground, 200,000 troops have been added. In addition, there are 1,000 aircraft, and an additional 100,000 infantry and cavalry, 1,000 airmen, and a large number of tanks will be mobilized to Manchuria. (Hua Lian News dispatch, 14th)

Three Islands in South Pacific Taken into US Territory, Located Between Hawaii and New Zealand, Will Become Important Aviation Stops in the Future

(Washington) The Pacific Intelligence Office today issued a statement announcing that Jarvis, Baker, and Howland Islands in the South Pacific will henceforth be formally incorporated into US territory. Dowell, the Customs Collector of Honolulu, has stipulated that those who travel to these three islands and return to Honolulu will not be subject to customs inspection, as it is considered that they have not left British territory. The Intelligence Office also stated that for eight months, four American citizens from the Hawaiian Islands have been living on each of the three islands to establish US territorial rights, and these three islands may become important stops on the Pacific air route in the future. As for the position of the three islands, they are located on the route between Hawaii and Australia and New Zealand. The situation on the islands has been thoroughly investigated by representatives of the US Department of Commerce. According to recent news, a US airline has reached an agreement with the British side to operate an air route from Hawaii to New Zealand in order to connect with the route operated by the British side from Australia through India to Britain. (National News Agency dispatch, 13th)

US Airship Achieves Final Successful Test Flight, Total Distance 6,400 Miles, Far East Route to Be Launched Soon

(San Francisco) The Pan American Airways Clipper, which departed from Alameda, California, on October 5 for a test flight to Guam, arrived safely at its destination tonight at 9:10 p.m. (Pacific time). An airman expressed the opinion that the route of the airship through Hawaii, Midway Island, and Wake Island can be used for regular postal and passenger air services across the Pacific Ocean between the United States and the Far East. The total distance is 6,478 miles, stopping at Hawaii after 2,400 miles, then stopping at Midway Island after 1,380 miles, then to Wake Island from Midway Island for 1,248 miles, and then another 1,450 miles to reach Guam. The flight completed today is believed to be the Clipper's final test flight, and regular air services to Manila or extended to China will be launched soon. If Manila is the terminus, the total distance will increase to 7,978 miles, and if it is extended to Guangzhou, it will increase by another 700 miles. Pan American Airways was launched in 1928, with a route of only 251 miles in the first year, which has increased to 32,252 miles last year. The speed of its development is evident. (Reuters dispatch, 13th)

Germany's Break with League of Nations Takes Effect Yesterday, Interior Minister's Speech Criticizes International Community

Saarbrücken. Germany's withdrawal from the League of Nations took effect yesterday. Interior Minister Frick delivered an important speech here today to celebrate the withdrawal from the League of Nations, saying, "Although the League of Nations claims to create peace and national coordination, it has never fulfilled this task. On the contrary, it is no exaggeration to say that the League of Nations is the source and catalyst of the Second World War. At this moment, the whole world is filled with war cries, and there is turmoil everywhere, but our Germany lives in an atmosphere of absolute calm." Frick then declared that Führer Hitler will visit the Saar soon, and the government will soon take legal measures to restrict the economic activities of Jews so that various individual anti-Jewish actions will not occur again. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

International Commercial Telegraph

——Special Commercial News Telegraph from Reuters, October 14——

Gold and Silver. British gold rose half a penny today to 141 shillings, 9 and a half pence.

British Silver. Trading in the silver market today remained slow. The spot price is 29.375 pence, and the forward price is 29.4375 pence, both the same as the price on Saturday. The United States bought in, and China sold out.

Exchange Rates. US-UK. The foreign exchange market was sluggish this morning. The opening price for US-UK exchange was $4.92125, which was .0625 lower than the closing price for US-UK exchange on Saturday. There were no changes afterwards.

French-UK. The opening price for French-UK exchange rose 1 pound sterling from the closing price on Saturday to 74 francs, 41. There were no changes afterwards.

Cotton and Wheat.

US Cotton. The price of cotton rose 8 pounds sterling due to large demand, but later fell back 1 or 2 pounds sterling, but there were very few short sellers. The foreign news was good, so people's minds continued to be stable.

US Wheat. The Chicago wheat market opened down 1.25, and the Liverpool wheat market rose. However, due to many short sellers, it fell again by 50 shortly after the opening. Due to the influence of the wheat market, grains opened down .25, and then continued to fall due to short selling.

British Wheat. Although the wheat market was loose on Saturday, it was steady today. In the afternoon, it rose a quarter of a penny to 6 shillings, 5 and a bit pence.

British Cotton. The opening price of the cotton market rose slightly. At 1:00 p.m., the January price was 6.09 pence, which was 3 pounds sterling higher than the weekend closing price.

Rubber. London rubber opened firm, with the March price still at 6.375 pence. At noon, there were still people buying at this price.

New York. The opening price of rubber in New York fell 1 pound sterling from the weekly technical, but soon rose back 2 pounds sterling. Although the price fell, the market situation was firm and stable.

Securities. New York. Securities all opened higher, and the psychology of blue-chip operators was stable. The average price of the Dow Jones 30 industrial stocks was 134.09, up 53 pounds sterling.

US Secretary of War Arrives in Tokyo, Will Visit Japanese Dignitaries, Not Discuss Politics

Yokohama: US Secretary of War Dern arrived here at 8:30 this morning aboard a US warship from the United States to participate in the founding celebrations of the Republic of the Philippines. Representatives of the Japanese government, US Chargé d'Affaires in Japan Neville, and other personnel from the embassy welcomed him. Mr. Dern will meet with the Japanese Emperor tomorrow and will also visit the Japanese Foreign Minister and Army Minister. Mr. Dern will stay in Japan for four days. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

(Tokyo) US Secretary of War Dern arrived in Tokyo from Yokohama and entered the US Embassy. According to reports, this visit to Japan is not an official one, so he does not wish to discuss political or diplomatic issues when meeting with Foreign Minister Hirota or Army Minister Kawashima. (United Press dispatch, 14th)

Yokohama: The US cruiser "Chester" (10,000 tons), carrying US Secretary of War Dern, his wife, son, and five military officers, and the French Far East Fleet flagship "Primauguet" (7,429 tons) arrived here one after the other at 8:00 AM today. US Ambassador to Japan Grew and others went to the pier to welcome them. Secretary Dern said that this was his first visit to Japan and that he had no other purpose in arriving in Hong Kong. He would go to the embassy immediately and visit the Ministry of Foreign Affairs tomorrow. All actions would be decided by the embassy. It was also reported that the arrival of the French "Primauguet" was due to the appointment of Vice Admiral D'Argenlieu as Commander of the Far East Fleet, who was paying a special visit to Japan. The ship carried 30 officers and 600 sailors and was scheduled to stay for two periods of time. (Dentsu dispatch, 14th)

Economic Study Mission to Japan Leaves Tokyo for Osaka

(Tokyo) The Chinese Industrial Inspection Group rested this morning and attended a luncheon hosted by Foreign Minister Hirota at the Foreign Ministry's vice-ministerial residence at 12:30 PM. Afterwards, they went to a tea party at the residence of Mr. Fujita Leitaro in Shirokanedai, Shiba. With this, the formal itinerary of the group was completed. They left Tokyo for Osaka at 9:00 PM tonight and will stay in Osaka and Kyoto until the 19th. On the 19th, they will go to Nara via 110 and then to Nagoya. The next day, the 21st, they will return to Tokyo in the evening. (Dentsu dispatch, 14th)

Japan Decides on Policy Towards Naval Conference, Opposes Exclusive Discussion of Qualitative Issues

(Tokyo) According to responsible sources, the Japanese government's response to the British naval proposal has been formally approved by the cabinet and will be sent out this week. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

(Tokyo) Since Britain proposed holding a naval disarmament conference this year, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Navy have been discussing the contents of the response to Britain. As the opinions of the two ministries recently became consistent, the Ministry of the Army was notified on the 14th, and after obtaining approval from the cabinet on the 15th, a formal reply will be sent to the British government. It is reported that the main points of the reply document decided by the Ministry of the Navy and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs are as follows:

(1) The Japanese government insists on its policy of realizing substantive disarmament among the world's major naval powers. Therefore, the demands of the Japanese government, advocated since the London Preliminary Talks in December last year, have not changed. (2) That is, Japan opposes the unilateral declaration of shipbuilding advocated by the United Kingdom to stipulate the amount of warships possessed by each country. Moreover, regarding only qualitative disarmament, Japan has no choice but to oppose making this qualitative issue the subject of the disarmament conference because there is no possibility of substantive disarmament. (3) Regarding the issue of holding a disarmament conference, Japan has previously sent representatives to attend the conference because the treaty already has regulations. (United Press dispatch, 14th)

New Life in the Capital, Labor Service Corps

(Nanjing) Preparations for the New Life Labor Service Corps of the Capital New Movement are complete. The corps consists of more than 2,600 members of the military police, students, and other groups. The Course of the Smuggling Issue in Chaozhou and Shantou, Seven Japanese Ships Still Stationed in Shantou, National Day Parade Therefore Suspended

Shantou Correspondence: During this year's Double Ten Festival, celebrations and military parades were held in various parts of Guangdong Province. In Shantou, the event was held at the Qilu airfield, with Li Hanhun as the reviewing officer and Luo Xianxiang as the commander. In Chao'an, the event was held at the West Lake Sports Ground, with Deng Longguang as the reviewing officer. In Meixian, the event was held at the East Drill Ground, with Huang Renhuan as the reviewing officer. In Xingning, the event was held at the Fangba Dam, with Tan Langxing as the reviewing officer. In Xunwu, the event was held at the Sanbiao market, with Zhang Ruigui as the reviewing officer. The garrisons in Jieyang, Fengshun, Dapu, and Raoping counties also held similar events. Boy scouts, militia, and regular troops from various schools all participated in the parade. However, the Shantou Preparatory Committee also planned to imitate the Guangzhou carnival and prepared for a scene-setting event, lion dances, dragon welcomes, fish lantern races, gongs and drums, horse scenes, paper scenes, human scenes, etc. All the expenses were specially collected from shops and residents, and were paid for by collecting taxes from various merchants. The amount was originally not small, and the preparations were ready, but unexpectedly the smuggling issue occurred? Japanese warships arrived in Shantou and demanded the release of people and goods, compensation for losses, and a guarantee that similar incidents would not occur in the future. They also declared that the fleet would not leave Shantou unless a satisfactory answer was given. Therefore, in order to avoid disputes, the authorities specially ordered the suspension of the parade on the 8th, and the grand event that was being prepared was virtually eliminated. However, at 8:30 AM on the 10th, representatives from various groups in Shantou, government officials, and military police students participating in the parade still gathered at the airfield, totaling more than 5,000 people. At 10:00 AM, cannons were fired to open the meeting. Li Hanhun, Li Yuanhe, and others went to the rostrum to perform the opening ceremony and gave brief speeches, and then the meeting was dismissed. This shows the current environment in Shantou.

The so-called smuggling issue is extremely complicated. Since Guangdong Province began collecting taxes on agricultural products, the taxes on oil, rice, beans, bean cakes, etc. have been particularly heavy. Japanese merchants do not recognize local taxes and have repeatedly transported large amounts of rice, oil, and beans from foreign ports. After declaring taxes at customs, they transport the goods to foreign firms' warehouses and hand them over to inland merchants for sale. The foreign firms guarantee the goods to the store and then pay the silver. If there is a loss due to detention or seizure after reaching the store, it is still the responsibility of the foreign firm. The foreign firms claim that the goods are consigned. Since this trend began, Chinese commercial firms, such as north-south firms and grain firms, have suffered a major blow. The Miansu Chang, opened by Cai Shifan, chairman of the north-south firms, was also affected and closed down. Currently, nearly 90% of them are closed. This is because each bag of rice has to pay more than four yuan in special tax, Shantou has to pay 5.4 yuan per 100 catties, soybeans have to pay 1.8 yuan per 100 catties, and other items such as old newspapers and seafood are all imported in large quantities by foreign firms. The cost of Chinese merchants' goods is high, so they naturally cannot compete with them. The Chaozhou-Shantou Chamber of Commerce and various guilds telegraphed the government two months ago requesting relief and asking to stop collecting various special taxes, special taxes, surcharges, etc., but the government rejected the request because the tax revenue is related to military salaries, which amount to 10 to 20 million yuan each year. Later, a strict method was devised: when Chinese merchants import oil, rice, and beans that have already paid taxes to the Agricultural Products Bureau, they must obtain a transportation permit from the tax bureau when selling them. This permit must be carried with the goods and presented to customs checkpoints along the way for inspection and release, and an inspection stamp must be obtained. With these two documents, the goods can be transported and sold inland; otherwise, they will be confiscated and punished. Although these procedures are troublesome, they are a new way to crack down on smuggled goods. On the 8th of last month, the Eastern District Commissioner's Office convened a meeting of responsible persons from military, political, police, tax, and anti-smuggling agencies and decided to work together to maintain tax revenue. At the same time, they telegraphed the county magistrates to cooperate in anti-smuggling. The counties also notified the district chiefs, township chiefs, autonomous regions, police teams, public security bureaus, and police stations to cooperate in the investigation. The anti-smuggling soldiers are responsible for the execution. On the 10th and 11th of last month, Jieyang County Magistrate Huang Bingxun sent police to search for smuggled goods. In Yanhefa outside the West Gate, 20 bags of black beans and 50 bags of soybeans were found. In Yongxinglong outside the North Gate, 110 bags of foreign rice were found. On the Beixi River surface, a five-bellied boat was found with 25 bags of foreign rice, 105 bags of green soybeans, and 80 barrels of soybean oil. Since the above shops did not have transfer slips and along-the-way inspection certificates, the police soldiers considered them smuggled goods and arrested many people related to the smuggled goods. According to the boat manager Zhang Zhenshu, the goods were transported by people from Qianjinhu in the 8th district of Puning and belonged to Youli, Daoli, Quanli, Yuda, Houfeng and other shops in Hepo market, and were entrusted to Zhang Quanchang from Jieyang to import them in Shantou. Based on this, County Magistrate Huang detained the relevant people. On the 12th, he convened many people, such as workers from the Civilian Boat Labor Union, and representatives from the Oil, Bean, and Oil Industry Guild, at the County Chamber of Commerce, instructing the Chamber of Commerce to notify all merchants to understand the righteousness, and all workers to love the country. If smuggling is encountered, they must not be greedy for money. Once it is discovered, they will be punished according to law. This case has provoked Japanese intervention. Seven Japanese warships have sailed into Shantou under the pretext of protecting overseas Chinese, and Japanese sailors have landed on the shore. This incident is getting more and more serious. Guangzhou and Nanjing both believe that the Chaozhou-Shantou issue is a companion, and the Japanese also believe that Chaozhou-Shantou is their common opponent. However, Jieyang is not within the Shantou municipal area, and Mayor Li Yuanhe has no power to investigate. The Eastern District Commissioner's Office does not have any negotiators, so Guangzhou will send another senior official to Shantou to be responsible for handling this case. It is reported that Gan Jiehou, Wu Bosheng, and Liang Zhihuai will arrive in Shantou during the day. The headquarters has also sent Li Jingxi, the head of the military law office, to Shantou to investigate and try the relevant criminals in the case. How this case will be resolved is currently unclear. (11th)

Chinese Economic Study Mission Arrives in Tokyo via Nagasaki, Hirota Hopes for Mutual Sincerity Between the Two Countries, Wu Dingchang Denies Various Reports in Japanese Newspapers

Tokyo Correspondence: The Chinese economic delegation to Japan arrived in Nagasaki at 12:00 noon on the 7th aboard the Shanghai Maru. The governor of Nagasaki Prefecture, the mayor, and our consul Liu stationed there were all waiting at the shore in advance. With the permission of the Ministry of the Navy, they accompanied the delegation to visit the Mitsubishi Shipyard after their arrival. Wu Dingchang, the head of the delegation, issued a written statement explaining the delegation's mission (original text follows). After a short stay, they set sail from Nagasaki at 5:00 PM. They arrived in Kobe at 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 8th. The mayor of Kobe specially hung the Chinese flag on Mount Anchor to express his welcome. Many Chinese and Japanese officials and businessmen welcomed them on the shore, creating a grand scene. After disembarking, they were hosted by the local Sino-Japanese Industrial Cooperation Association and a welcome party was held at the Chamber of Commerce and Industry. Important Chinese and Japanese officials and businessmen in Kobe attended. The mayor, the president of the Sino-Japanese Industrial Cooperation Association, Longchuan, and the president of the Chamber of Commerce and Industry, Okazaki, delivered welcome speeches. Delegation leader Wu Dingchang gave a speech in reply (original text follows). Afterwards, he also issued a written statement (original text follows). Then, at about 8:00 PM, they took a night train east. At 8:00 AM on the morning of the 9th, they arrived at Tokyo Station. Ambassador Chiang and representatives from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Councilor Matsumoto, the president of Yokohama Specie Bank, Toratama, the president of the Bank of Chosen, Kato, the president of the Chamber of Commerce and Industry, Wata Makoto, and more than 100 representatives from Chinese and Japanese circles, including embassy staff, welcomed them at the station. They then went to the Imperial Hotel and stayed there. The head of the delegation also issued a written statement explaining the delegation's mission and his personal feelings (original text follows). At about 9:00 AM, they went to the embassy, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, Ministry of Commerce and Industry, Chamber of Commerce and Industry, Sino-Japanese Industrial Association and other places to pay their respects. In the afternoon, they rested together at the hotel. At 7:00 PM, Ambassador Chiang hosted a banquet at the Imperial Hotel to welcome all the members of the delegation, and invited Foreign Minister Hirota, Minister of Agriculture Yamasaki, Minister of Commerce Machida, and major leaders from the Japanese industrial community to participate. Ambassador Chiang first delivered a speech at the meeting, stating that "Your Excellencies have come to Japan to conduct research, representing various provinces and major cities in China, and have in-depth research on the situation in Japan. This is a rare occasion. In addition to expressing my welcome and admiration, I will do my best to introduce you to various parties here and in Korea, so as to fulfill the meaning of your coming here. At the same time, I hope that people from all walks of life in Japan will provide you with convenience and assistance." Then Wu Dingchang gave a reply (original text follows). Hirota then stood up and gave a speech, saying, "I very much welcome you to our country to conduct research. However, the matters of research are all under the jurisdiction of the Minister of Commerce and Industry and should be spoken by the Minister of Commerce and Industry. But my family was originally a merchant, so I am also interested in commerce. And today's host is a diplomat and a good friend, so I am able to talk with you as the Foreign Minister. It is very pleasant." Then he quoted Confucius, hoping that people from both countries would treat each other with sincerity, which would be fortunate for the future of the relationship between the two countries. Then they talked to each other until about 10 o'clock, and then dispersed in joy. This was the situation on the first day after the delegation arrived in Tokyo. According to a conversation with Wu Dingchang, the head of the delegation, the delegation had not expressed any opinions other than the written statements issued since its departure. The reports in the Japanese newspapers were not true and were fabricated freely. The written statements issued by the delegation are appended below.

Speech Delivered in Nagasaki: Our delegation feels that it is very meaningful to visit Nagasaki, the birthplace of international trade in your country, as the first step on our research trip. Nagasaki is a major trading port closest to our country, and there are many Chinese residents. If time permits, we plan to conduct a more detailed investigation on the way back. Today, due to the short mooring time, we were only able to visit the Mitsubishi Shipyard with the kindness of your country's Maritime Affairs Ministry. As for the mission of our delegation, it is to inspect the prosperous commercial and industrial enterprises of Japan today as a national economic service provider, in order to realize economic cooperation between the two countries. I am fortunate to be able to state the mission of our delegation on this first opportunity to land in Nagasaki, the birthplace of international trade in your country. I sincerely hope that you will appreciate the purpose of our delegation and give your support.

Speech Delivered in Kobe: Our delegation visited Nagasaki, the birthplace of international trade in your country, as the first step of this research trip yesterday. Today, we have arrived in Kobe, the gateway to the industrial center, as the second step, and we feel that we are progressing step by step. Hanshin occupies a thousand seats in your country's industrial zone. In terms of order, we should have inspected it first. I only believe that due to various business negotiations, we decided to go to Tokyo first. Because this inspection of our delegation is not for sightseeing, but has a collaborative mission, we are waiting for the assistance of all parties for the common development of the economies of the two countries.

Speech Delivered upon Arrival in Tokyo: In the past, there have been various study missions from our country to this place, and their purpose was to take Tokyo as the center of their inspection. Therefore, there are many aspects that disturb the local government and the public. However, this is truly worth celebrating in the diplomatic relations between Japan and China. If the people of the two countries have more contact, their mutual understanding can be clarified. Understanding can be sufficient, and this can promote national diplomacy in the true sense of the word and Sino-Japanese friendship. Today, our delegation also has this view, gathers many members, and disturbs your country. The special mission of our delegation, as its name suggests, is economic research. However, the so-called research is not to investigate the advantages of your country's economic circles for the reference of our country's economic circles. It is not a one-sided, selfish meaning. It is to investigate your country's economic circles and our country's economic circles, what good plans should be used to help each other and cooperate to be the foundation of economic cooperation between the two countries. This is the so-called two-sided, mutual meaning. Therefore, during our stay, we plan to meet with knowledgeable people in the government and the public, visit various commercial and industrial facilities, and collect various materials in accordance with this purpose. We sincerely hope that all parties will provide assistance and cooperation. Furthermore, this is my fourth visit. The first time was in 1902, for the purpose of studying abroad. The second time was in 1915, when I was the head of an industrial delegation and led a number of members. I had arrived in Gyeongseong, Korea, but was suddenly advised to stop by your country due to certain special circumstances, so I turned back halfway. The third time was in 1928, when I came as a representative to the Pacific Conference. Each of these visits had different feelings and missions, but this trip is different from the past and I feel a sense of worldly isolation. At the same time, I deeply feel the importance of the mission, just like when I was studying abroad, I came to listen to textbooks, and now I feel that I have come to answer application questions. Whether the answer in the future will be correct or wrong is uncertain.

Speech at the Embassy Banquet: Your Excellency Ambassador Chiang, Your Excellencies, and Gentlemen, I am very grateful to Ambassador Chiang for hosting a grand banquet to introduce distinguished Japanese figures from the government and the public on the evening of the day our delegation arrived in Tokyo. I am especially honored to be able to take this opportunity to express my thoughts on behalf of the delegation to Your Excellencies and Gentlemen. Since the European War, people in Chinese economic circles have deeply known that Japanese commercial and industrial circles have made world-class rapid development, and have especially deeply felt the expansion of the cooperative economic forces among countries in the world. There is an even greater need for economic cooperation between China and Japan. For a long time, we have been thinking of organizing a joint study mission of various industries in various places to visit and inspect Japan's rapidly developing commercial and industrial enterprises, so as to promote economic cooperation between the two countries. The ambition has not been one day, and the sincerity has not been one day. Once this opportunity is obtained, all members of the delegation are happy to celebrate. Originally, economic cooperation between the two countries must hope for the efforts of the governments of the two countries, but how can the people of the two countries give up their responsibilities? They must do their best to promote it. Although the members of our delegation are weak, they are also willing to stand on their shoulders and share some responsibilities. Therefore, we plan to inspect commercial and industrial enterprises on the one hand, exchange economic opinions on the other hand, and plan to conduct continuous research and efforts in the future, so as to inevitably obtain appropriate and feasible concrete plans and complete the great cause of economic cooperation between the two countries. Therefore, I sincerely request the comrades of Japan's government and public to give our delegation convenience, support, and guidance, so that the members of our delegation can bring back the good intentions of Japan's government and public for economic cooperation between the two countries. I respectfully state my humble intentions and express my gratitude in advance. (October 10)

Japan Electric Communication Company's Economic Observation Group Arrives in Jinan, Departs for Tianjin After One-Day Stay; Group Leader Discusses Purpose of Visit

Jinan Communication: To commemorate the 30th anniversary of Japan's Electric Communication Company (Denstu), a Chinese economic observation group was specially organized. The group, consisting of 14 members including Mishima Kaiun, arrived in Jinan early on the 13th from Qingdao.伴野韶光, the branch manager of the company's Qingdao branch and concurrently the Jinan branch manager, accompanied them. The Japanese Consul in Jinan, 西田, the military attaché 石野, and leaders of the expatriate community all welcomed them at the station. After disembarking, the group immediately went to the Hejia Hotel to rest. According to group leader Mishima Kaiun, "This time, our group is here to investigate the economy of your country under the auspices of the Electric Communication Company. Besides three members from the Electric Communication Company, there are also eleven others: five from Tokyo, four from Osaka, and one from Nagoya. Among them are 鈴本宇一, the deputy chief of the editorial bureau of the Tokyo Hochi Shimbun, 目畸憲司, a doctor of economics from the general affairs department of the Sumitomo Gomei Kaisha, and the remaining seven are all from the industrial and commercial sectors. The purpose of this trip is that we are not very familiar with the economic situation and rural conditions in various parts of your country, and we hope to conduct a detailed investigation to provide reference for industry and commerce. After arriving in Qingdao, the surface scenery we saw was beautiful and very pleasing to the eye, but upon investigating the inner workings, industry and commerce are still in need of development. The shortage of water in Qingdao greatly affects industry. If the water supply were sufficient, factories would certainly develop further. Shandong's climate is suitable for two harvests a year, while the weather in Northeast Manchuria is cold, and there is only one harvest a year. Therefore, although Shandong is smaller than Manchuria, its production is not small, and its future is very promising. Our country is an industrial country, and China is a raw material country. Not only must China supply raw materials, but the industrial products produced must also be purchased by Chinese farmers. However, unless Chinese agricultural production develops, it cannot supply Japanese industry, and unless the Chinese rural economy recovers, farmers will not be able to afford Japanese goods. Therefore, we very much hope that Chinese agriculture will develop, so that both China and Japan can benefit from it. Japanese industry and commerce are relatively developed, and we very much hope that various circles in China will organize observation groups to visit. The Japanese government and people will sincerely welcome them. As for the issue of investment, it must be Manchuria first and then Shandong. Currently, the order in Manchuria is not yet fully established, and Japanese large capitalists have not yet made large investments. Those who have invested are all small capitalists. In the future, investment in Shandong can only begin after investment in Manchuria is successful," and so on.

The group's itinerary in Jinan: Arrived in Jinan at 7:30 AM on the 13th, rested at the Hejia Hotel, had breakfast at 8:00 AM, visited the Japanese Consul 西田 at 9:00 AM, paid respects to the Japanese War Dead Monument at 10:00 AM, and visited the Japanese military attaché, the Japanese Residents' Association, the Japanese elementary school, Jinan Hospital, the Japanese Chamber of Commerce and Industry, the Chinese Jinan Chamber of Commerce, and Jinan Bank.
