Spring and Autumn

Foreign Exchange Supply Exceeds Demand; Japanese Banks Sell English Currency, Korean Banks Sell English Currency… Chinese Banks Sell American Currency on the Mainland

According to yesterday's foreign dispatches, the American market was entirely closed. Only in London were short-term and long-term transactions close to par. Forward silver prices in Menterri remained unchanged. London spot gold dropped by half a penny. The British pound rose 1.25 against the US dollar and remained unchanged against the French franc. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with the near-term selling price of the British pound at one shilling and six pence and one-eighth. The US dollar was at 37.0625 yuan. Compared with last Saturday, the British pound and the US dollar were level. Market sentiment was weak, trending towards easing after opening. The Central Bank's posted rates were announced, with the British pound and the US dollar both level. Customs gold units also remained unchanged. Banks took advantage of the low prices to buy in, immediately stabilizing the market. However, the selling by Japanese and Mainland banks was difficult to sustain. It was anticipated that the HSBC Bank's posted rates would keep the British pound and the US dollar both level. At this point, to balance supply and demand, Sassoon and others slightly bought in and hovered. However, Chinese banks such as Bank of Communications and Continental Bank continued to supply, and market sentiment remained weak, eventually strengthening again. It was predicted that Indian silver would fall by one anna. At noon, it slightly turned peaceful. Later in the market, although banks continued to sell, Chinese merchants suddenly competed to buy in, resulting in an oversupply that gradually strengthened the market. The initial quote for Indian silver was one anna, and the Hong Kong market softened, becoming tighter. However, banks took advantage of the high prices to sell together, stabilizing the situation. Later, Indian silver rebounded to four annas in the second quote, briefly turning level, but ultimately maintained its position. The closing near-term selling price for the British pound was one shilling and six pence and a quarter, and the US dollar was at 37.25 yuan. Compared to last Saturday, the British pound eased by one-eighth and the US dollar hardened by 0.1875. Chinese merchants bought in about 100,000 US dollars. Japanese and Korean banks sold English currency, and Chinese banks sold American currency on the mainland. The transaction records for today are listed below.

The British pound opened in the morning with a near-term selling price of one shilling and six pence and one-eighth. Korea sold one-eighth for October to McCallie. Korea sold 0.25 for spot to Illies and HSBC. Banque Belge pour l'Étranger sold 0.125 for October to Shanghai Sassoon. Korea sold 0.25 for spot to Banque Belge pour l'Étranger. HSBC bought in 5 pence and 6875/10000 for December. The noon closing near-term selling price was one shilling and six pence and a quarter. Later in the market, Bombay sold 5 pence and 6875/10000 for December to Illies. McCallie sold 6 pence and 125/1000 for October to Bombay. Citibank sold 5 pence and 6875/10000 for December to Chase, and Bombay sold the same to Banque Belge pour l'Étranger. The closing selling price was one shilling and six pence and a quarter for spot, one-eighth for October, 5 pence and 875/10000 and 9375/10000 for November paired, 6875/10000 for December, and a halfpenny for January. The buying price added 0.0625.

The US dollar opened in the morning with a near-term selling price of 37.0625 yuan. McCallie and Chase bought in 6.5 yuan for November, and Mitsui sold at the same price for the same month. Continental sold 5.625 yuan for November. McCallie bought in 7.0625 yuan for October. Bank of Communications and Continental sold 6.5 yuan for November. Continental sold 5.625 yuan for the same month to Shanghai. Citibank sold at the same price for the same month. The noon closing near-term selling price was 37.13125 yuan. Later in the market, Continental sold 6.5625 yuan for November. McCallie and Citibank sold 0.0625 yuan for December. Shanghai sold 0.5 yuan for November to British Bank. Interbank Loan Rate Unchanged; Double Dime Coins Firm and Stable

Yesterday (Monday), the interbank loan rate for foreign currency remained at 13% in both the morning and afternoon markets. Checks for transfer were also used in vain. In terms of interbank loan transactions, over 3.8 million was transferred in the morning market, with over 400,000 in new transactions. In the afternoon market, transactions amounted to 600,000, and transactions within the Small Clearing House totaled over 500,000. Although the head-of-line funds were still abundant in the afternoon, checks for transfer were ultimately used in vain. However, within the Small Clearing House, there was a slight clearance, resulting in a market of 2-3%. Transactions involving foreign currency pledges were slightly more active at 10%. The total amount of redemptions was over 900,000, and new loans amounted to over 1.3 million. 800,000 in banknotes were recovered, 400,000 in marked banknotes were issued, 900,000 in circulating banknotes, 400,000 from customer sources, and 250,000 from the "fu wei" (likely a typo for "fu wei", meaning "auxiliary"). Money shops and public banks received over 44.4 million, over 5.24 million in foreign exchange transfers, over 500,000 in remittances from various sources, and 400,000 in cash settlements. Banks received over 3.56 million in remittances from foreign banks, over 4.5 million in miscellaneous remittances for various goods and exchanges, 400,000 in telegraphic transfers, over 1.2 million in foreign exchange settlements, over 900,000 in special remittances, over 1.4 million in difference settlements, and 600,000 in warehouse receipts. Chinese banks received over 4.1 million in remittances, over 5.9 million in miscellaneous remittances for various goods and exchanges, over 1.34 million in foreign exchange settlements, over 800,000 in special remittances, over 1.8 million in difference settlements, and 700,000 in warehouse receipts. Japanese banks received over 3.3 million in remittances, over 4.3 million in miscellaneous remittances for various goods and exchanges, over 700,000 in special remittances, over 900,000 in foreign exchange settlements, and 500,000 in warehouse receipts.

Securities: Securities Suddenly Plunged Four Times Yesterday—A Rare Occurrence in Recent Months

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange experienced a sudden and major storm, with a very sharp decline. Various "gangs" vigorously sold, with No. 16 shorting additional shares and No. 54 longs liquidating. Selling was extremely enthusiastic. Others, such as Nos. 4, 46, and 69, also consistently sold. For a time, a strong selling atmosphere prevailed in the market. On the buying side were Nos. 14, 34, 64, and 72, but supply and demand were still unbalanced. No. 48, a long, was also still adding shares slightly. The market sentiment appeared somewhat panicked. The reason for this was entirely the shadow of terrifying rumors, undoubtedly closely related to the Dalian Conference. Yesterday, the market opened with a small drop of about 0.1 to 0.5 yuan. The trend still felt even. In the second round, selling was even more intense, and the decline became increasingly severe. The current month plummeted 0.7 yuan. When the afternoon market opened, the selling pressure was even greater. Quite a few longs from the morning turned short in the afternoon. Northern "gangs" further down the list slightly bought. As the price of Current Month contract Number 6 returned one jiao, the decline stopped at this point, but by closing time, the late evening news was bad. Number 11 sold Kuang Mai Tsai Ping, suddenly plummeting another 0.8 or 0.9 yuan. After this the decline moderated somewhat, but still fell 0.3, 0.5 or 0.6 yuan. The fall was too violent, and there may be a small reversal. The resulting market price fell approximately one yuan to six yuan. The total volume traded was approximately 30 million yuan. The cotton yarn market continued to decline, and the situation deteriorated further. Various rumors flew about in the local area, and the various stories were inconsistent, making it difficult for people to feel at ease. Cotton prices loosened, and the selling atmosphere became slightly stronger. However, the current yarn situation remained profitable due to the tight fundamental situation. Selling prices did not fall, and merchants from Sichuan made considerable purchases.

The prices of graded yarn declined in both morning and afternoon sessions.

The graded yarn market opened in the morning, with prices declining across all months. Rumors spread, benefiting the shorts. The selling atmosphere in the market was particularly strong, with prices declining by 7, 8, and 9 jiao across all months. After 2 o'clock, there was little change. By closing, news came that Osaka's Sanpin cotton yarn had risen sharply by 2-3 yuan, slightly stimulating the sluggish yarn market and pushing prices back up by a few jiao. As a result, prices for all months still fell by 3, 4, 5, and 6 jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. The afternoon session opened with a flat and weak tone. The market sentiment was very loose and became softer as the auction progressed, entirely due to the attack of rumors. As a result, prices for all months fell by 2, 4, 7, 8, and 9 jiao to 1 yuan compared to the morning closing price. Oil Market: Theory that Tung Oil Production is High This Year

After the standard-weight white tung oil had its stock sold off, many of the non-standard-weight goods were purchased by foreign firms in the Hankou market. However, because prices rose too much, the reaction was also strong. Recently, because US prices fell sharply, the Hankou foreign firms have all stopped doing business. The price of futures for the past 12 months once peaked at 70 yuan per report, but recently has fallen to 60 yuan, and the foreign firms still do not greedily take it. Although the current price has no official market price, it is being secretly brewed. The new oil in each producing area has started to be pressed, and the day the new oil reaches Hankou is near. In the future, the new goods can also be assessed at the current market price of 60 yuan. Once they open, a sudden drop of 0.1 to 0.2 yuan in the market will happen, which is shocking. If one is not cautious with this kind of market condition, one can easily be impacted by it. It is a misfortune for those engaged in this business. Therefore, there are very few new oil transactions, because the market price has not been on the right track. Those who want to do business do not dare to touch it. Even if the price falls to between 50 and 60 yuan, it is still a high price, and the weather is very hot this year. According to someone who did an investigation in the Zhejiang area, the output is said to have doubled compared to previous years.

Free Talk

Concerning Intellectuals

— Gan Nu

Mr. Cao Juren has recently been very dismissive of intellectuals. I remember him expressing sentiments like "Scholars are useless," and now in his article "Rectifying the Mildew of the May Fourth Movement" (Free Talk, October 8th), he said the following:

I feel that intellectuals are the least reliable. They are good at righteous indignation, but also the most likely to sell themselves. Liang Qichao praised Yang Du as the most spirited youth, but it was he who placed Yuan Shikai on the emperor's throne. Zhao Xinbo, who was a leader of the patriotic movement in Shanghai, is now a top-ranking traitor there. As Huang Yuansheng himself described, he went as a student representative to apply for the so-called "despotic" Nanyang Public School. The most dangerous thing about the drifting consciousness of intellectuals is depicting the student representatives of the May Fourth Movement as pure social activists. That is most dangerous...too few student representatives are willing to serve society from beginning to end!

It is well known that intellectuals are prone to change due to their social status; it goes without saying. What Bi Xue points out is Mr. Cao's assertion of "the least reliable," mainly referring to first being "filled with righteous indignation," and then "selling oneself," not "being willing to serve society from beginning to end," meaning turning bad. Of course, there is some merit to these words. For example, it can teach those outside the intellectual class to rely on their own strength when engaging in any movement, not to blindly trust intellectuals, to constantly monitor and urge them, and to prevent the regression and betrayal of intellectuals and their own deception. At the same time, it can also alert intellectuals themselves, strengthen their determination, and overcome their weaknesses.

However, Mr. Cao seems to portray the corruption of intellectuals as something predestined, irredeemable, and all-encompassing. If the corruption of intellectuals is predestined, we need not offer our enthusiasm for any movement, let alone overcome our own inferior nature, because it is impossible to save them anyway. It would be better for everyone to know their place and "sell themselves" directly. If all intellectuals are unreliable, the masses should, of course, completely disregard their intellectual stars and drive these "non-one-of-us" fellows out of the ranks as soon as possible. If this interpretation is permissible, Mr. Cao's opinion is dangerous enough.

First of all, the intellectual Mr. Cao refers to is just an abstract noun. From this noun, apart from knowing that they have knowledge, we get nothing else. What kind of knowledge is it? What is the living environment of a particular intellectual? Without understanding these conditions, it is too early to determine whether he is reliable or not. For example, Zheng Xiaoxu, the former Prime Minister of "Manchukuo," is he not an intellectual? Is Lin Yutang, the "master," not also an intellectual? One was a "top-ranking" traitor in "Manchukuo," and the other lived in the Republic of China, praising the ancestors of the "Manchukuo" king, the traitor "Lord Zeng Wenzheng." In Mr. Cao's view, this is, of course, confirmation of their "unreliability." But isn't the ability to "entrust a six-foot orphan, to entrust a hundred-mile fate," protecting the young ruler and reviving the country, exhausting all efforts, the highest expression of "a bit of solitary loyalty and integrity," that is, "barbarian spirit"? So, what Mr. Cao considers "unreliable" is precisely what Zheng "Prime Minister" takes pride in as "reliable," and what Lin "Master" admires as "reliable." Why is there such a difference in what each considers reliable? I think the answer should be sought from the knowledge itself, especially their living environment. At the same time, those intellectuals who have never been good, and therefore have no particular "corruption," need not be included in the lament.

Secondly, not all intellectuals are unreliable. Throughout history, many great leaders who emerged from mass movements were intellectuals. However, those who evade danger and betray friends for personal gain are often deliberately exaggerated and publicized, causing those with ulterior motives, like Mr. Cao, to shake their heads and sigh. As for the news of those who are unyielding, righteous, and generously sacrifice themselves, it is suppressed and stifled, so it cannot stimulate people's minds. At the same time, Mr. Cao's statement that they turned from "righteous indignation" to "selling themselves" only sees one side of intellectuals. On the other hand, there are also many intellectuals who turn from "selling themselves" to "righteous indignation." Of course, it is not easy for intellectuals to "serve society from beginning to end." Having come from "selling themselves" today, it is difficult to guarantee that they will not go back from "righteous indignation" tomorrow. The "drifting consciousness" of intellectuals is fostered by their drifting lives – drifting from work, from society, and from practice.

Furthermore, Mr. Cao underestimates the May Fourth Movement because he is dissatisfied with the later "selling out" of student representatives. This is wrong. The value of the May Fourth Movement should be estimated from the social significance contained in the movement itself, from the role it played in history, and not entirely on the personal behavior of a few student representatives. The student movement was only one wing of the May Fourth Movement, and student representatives were only a small part of those who participated in the student movement. The "selling out" of student representatives, unless it directly betrays the movement and strikes a blow to it, will not reduce the role that the movement can play, and the value of the movement itself will not be diminished. Moreover, the "selling out" that Mr. Cao refers to is about later events; it is not sufficiently justified to presume that he was not "pure" at the time because he "sold out" later. Mr. Cao seems to believe in Huang Yuansheng very much. Because Huang Yuansheng was "without principles, without ideals, without integrity," he also lacked understanding. He confused the social role of the entire movement with personal actions, and used the method of generalizing from the particular to make wrong estimates of student movements or revolutions. There is no time to elaborate on this here. But didn't he clearly say: "During the imperial examination era, I had no thought of becoming an official. When overseas students were about to graduate, the thought of making a living and the so-called patriotic thought were intertwined in my mind" (quoted from Mr. Cao's original text)? It can be seen that even if a person later has the so-called "thought of making a living," the previous "no thought of becoming an official" can also be absolutely true. Of course, I don't want to defend the "selling out" elements, nor do I want to deliberately exaggerate the significance of the May Fourth Movement. If we can prove from the development process of a certain student representative that his "selling out" has some causal relationship with the May Fourth Movement, we can only say that the May Fourth Movement was originally just a social movement at a certain stage. When the social movement develops to a higher stage, the elements that originally participated in that movement cannot keep up with the progress of society, and then they decline. "Selling out" is just one of the manifestations of decline. It does not harm his original purity, nor does it harm the movement he participated in.

Finally, Mr. Cao said: "We ourselves should admit our mistakes like Huang Yuansheng, expose our own malignant syphilis, and not use nice words to cover it up!" This is very good. But it is only limited to the occasion of self-liquidation, as the beginning of a new direction. If one "admits mistakes" and is pessimistic, timid, and self-denying, then it will turn from "malignant syphilis" to incurable depression and cowardice. Nakedly "exposing one's own malignant syphilis" should be to bravely seek medical treatment. Otherwise, even if one does not hate the illness and commit suicide, there is nothing valuable about it. Moreover, since intellectuals are good at "using nice words to cover up," once the trend of "admitting mistakes" begins, who knows if someone will not use the good name of "admitting mistakes" to cover up themselves?

In short, it is well known that intellectuals are prone to wavering. However, believing that they will fatefully turn bad and giving them excessive contempt will only drive intellectuals into a dead end, which is also unnecessary.

Singapore Port (Middle)

— Liu Ming

The pockmarked young man raised his hand, gesturing for the old man to stand up.

The old man, still scrambling around, looked around, twitched the two wisps of his mustache, and asked:

"Are you talking nonsense? What good things would be here?"

"Pull it, who said here?" The pockmarked young man saw the old man had gone in, and quickly suppressed his laughter. "People are inviting you ashore to stroll around Chinatown, to eat at the Nan Tian Grand Restaurant!"

The old man saw the police guarding over there, and remembered he had been tricked again. His face reddened, and he cursed him with an ugly word.

The pockmarked young man, as if he hadn't had enough fun, straightened his waist towards the old man, patted his pocket, and shouted:

"What? Can't afford it?… There's plenty of money here!"

The old man showed a bitter smile, scratching his head as he said:

"Damn it, it's easy for you to talk pretty here. Go to the streets of Xiamen, then...try it."

His Burmese woman, though she didn't understand Chinese, could tell from their expressions that they were just joking around. She winked at the two children surrounding the lace curtain and nudged her lips towards the pockmarked young man. The two children, who loved to play with the pockmarked young man along the way, immediately ran over, grabbing his pockets one after the other, trying to snatch his money.

Just then, many people suddenly crowded towards the ship's railing (the side facing the sea), craning their necks to look down. The pockmarked young man pressed his pocket with his left hand, raised his right hand and waved, shouting, "Ha, ha, there, what? What? Go look," finally freeing himself.

"Miserly fellow!"

The old man cursed in dissatisfaction and finally squeezed over to look too.

It turned out that there were three or four Malays near the ship's side, wearing swimming trunks, bare-chested, each riding a very small boat, looking up at the white passengers standing by the first- and second-class cabins with smiling and pleading faces. One of them had just emerged from the light green sea, holding something he had picked up high above the water, making a show of it. Then, he put his hand to his ear and gave a grateful wave to the first- and second-class cabins. After a while, the white passengers in the first- and second-class cabins threw a shiny little thing into the sea. Immediately, two or three people paddling the boat dropped their oars and dived into the water like fish to grab it.

"What are they doing?"

The old man strained his eyes to look, nudging the person next to him with his elbow as he asked. The person wiped the sweat from his forehead, turned around and replied.

Honorable Wife (7)

— by Jiang Mashu, translated by Ren Jun

"What, I am Japanese! Even if my son died in battle, I would not be surprised or cry. That would be shameful. In our Japan, many mothers whose beloved sons are killed by others believe that they died for the country and let go of everything. However, my son has not died, he is still alive. I received a letter not long ago. He is fighting bravely with the Russian devils. There is really nothing more worthy of congratulations than this! Ha, ha, ha..."

Then, she seemed to deliberately shake her whole body, laughing wildly.

The old woman often ran to my mother with a smile on her face and said:

"Madam, I'm sorry, please lend me the "cat skin" again. I've been thinking about all sorts of things, and I want to play the samisen again."

The so-called "cat skin" refers to the samisen. After my mother readily lent her the samisen, she took it to the workers' dormitory in the factory, sat in the empty, floored room, and immediately began to play. Naturally, the tune was chaotic, just a random strumming. She also sang loudly in a mess. Then, I don't know if it was because she couldn't restrain her joy, or because she found it funny to be doing such a thing, she would often open her toothless red mouth and laugh out loud...

"Oh dear, she's started acting crazy again." Although the people at home pitied her, they couldn't help but frown.

"Poor thing," my mother muttered to herself, hearing the demonic music and laughter that came into her ears, "If her son died in battle, she would really go crazy. Namo Amitabha, please protect her from such a thing!"

Contrary to initial expectations, Lushunkou was not so easy to capture. The attacks became more and more fierce, and the war increased the degree of tragedy. Every day, soldiers sent from our region to fight were killed in action. Those who were happy and celebrating amidst the joy of victory were probably only those who had not sent a single soldier from their own relatives. As for the families of the soldiers who had gone to war, their hearts were disturbed by uneasy terror when they heard the extra issue of the newspaper, when they opened the newspaper, and when they talked about the wind and snow of war.

The cooking old woman's son was still fighting safely. Not only that, but he had recently been promoted to lance corporal for his merits. The old woman was very proud.

"What's going on!" She smiled, wrinkling her nose. "It's still my son who is amazing! I prayed to the gods and Buddhas, and thanks to the gods and Buddhas, my son didn't die, and he was even promoted to lance corporal. He's doing a great job. Maybe he won't die and will become a general and come back with a shiny golden rooster medal. Long live, long live!"

Ancient City

— Zigang

Moved again.

I really live under the old city wall. As long as I make a turn, I can see the gray city wall in the gray alley. When a gust of wind passes, it drags up a large cloud of smoke, covering my eyes as if they are separated by many layers of gauze.

I have seen tourists who have traveled here elsewhere. In their piles of photos, you can always find one or two photos of the city tower of this ancient city without disappointing you. It is so huge and so majestic that people cannot help but be suffocated by the oriental architecture and exclaim in admiration. How many people have constructed beautiful and magical dreams for this ancient city.

However, what a medieval decay is shown in front of me!

Scattered, broken, dull...

Because of the collapse, most of the steps beside the city gate are hung with signs that say "No Climbing". Or is there any deeper meaning besides preventing tourists from danger? But people can still find a path trodden by people over the years and sneak up. From there, you can see the spectacle of Peiping City! — Red walls, yellow tiles, and some newly built gray walls and green tiles, and in the distance, the mountains are buried in the clouds. Unfortunately, there are not so many vast rivers here. Even the one at the foot of the city is as thin as a ribbon. When it is hot and dry, a burst of stench will open with the wind, which will make people from water towns curse fiercely. Besides the inspectors and naughty tourists, those who come to the city head are the firm city dwellers who want to throw their lives down here. This has become news that is not new in people's ears.

Large vehicles are prohibited from passing on the asphalt road, so most of them have to pass through small alleys or walk around the city. The paths of heavy livestock and wheels are deeply stepped on in the thick soil. "People grow up from the soil," this sentence may not be wrong. Camel teams often pass by here too. The ancient city, the camel bells, don't they give people who breathe in dreams some longing?

It seems that there are few high-ranking families under the city gate. Which gentleman or young lady is willing to eat ashes here! Here, only dilapidated corpses or small houses that have never been raised are gathered together. The children squat on the ground all year round to play with mud, draw little people and little horses on the city walls, pick wildflowers that protrude from the brick cracks, and pick some wild jujubes in autumn. The children grow up with tears, laughter, words and curses.

At the foot of the city gate, there are always a few traces of yellow earth and new bricks on both sides, like stamps on envelopes stuck there. That was a defensive work during the incident four years ago. Trenches were dug and anti-aircraft guns were prepared to be erected there.

Walking out of the city, there are always small market-like stalls and vendors. The rickshaw pullers stand there eating enema and drinking hot soup. The barriers of the railway crossing are opened and closed again according to the time. The people and vehicles coming and going temporarily stop, watching the long train and the dusty faces revealed in the train windows.

Living at the foot of this city wall, the roar of the train when it passes by every day is the most moving music. What does it evoke and what does it take away.

Sunlight in Memory

— Wu Rangsan

At this time, I lived in Shanghai.

It's not a very good place. And the weather is bad, and my house is very bad. The sky is a chaotic lead-blue color, and the blurred clouds are kneaded into some ugly faces. It is always so ambiguous, swollen, and layer upon layer of gray is added, and it becomes more and more calm and sinister.

Occasionally, a few days a year, a powerless tube of sunlight will leak from the corner of the window, obliquely inserted on the wall or the yellow table painted with shellac, which is my greatest comfort. If not, if a person doesn't have sunlight even once a year, I don't think I can survive.

I jumped up and kissed it with my lips. It's like I've lost everything, and this is my only last possession. I put down everything else. Sleeping on the table, or leaning against the wall, closing my eyes, I faced it with my face, trying to draw it into my breath as much as possible. …Using a mirror to do the old trick. Carefully, patiently, bring the sunlight to every corner of the room, and get the satisfaction of burning something for real. Sometimes use a basin of water. Sometimes block it with your palm, and hide under your palm. …In short. Get my happiness in various ways. …

I used to have inexhaustible sunlight. I have never lived in a university, but piecing together those fragmented, intermittent elementary and middle school lives can also make up six or seven academic years. — The brilliant sunlight endlessly shines on my days.

On the contrary, I didn't cherish it at that time, and I didn't know what interest it would have in me. In the field, in the playground, in the corridor, I picked it up casually, and threw it away casually.

Now, I am very stingy in using it! Sometimes when I suddenly open my eyes to it, it stings me, and tears flow down. At this time, when I close my eyes, I think of the fact that I didn't know how to cherish it before.

I am not using sunlight to symbolize youth or anything else, that doesn't make much sense. For example, for youth, I think it can be borrowed from the power of true art to make it undiminished and exist more vigorously.

I just like to let it sting me, shed tears, and close my eyes, that kind of real happiness.

— by Huang Shiying

Father: May you bless my two children to enter heaven safely!

National Games Day 5: Shanghai Firmly Wins Three Track and Field Championships for Men and Women; Pole Vault and Women's Javelin Set New National Records; Track and Field Ends Today; All-Around Swimming Begins Tomorrow

Yesterday was the fifth day of the National Games. In the men's and women's track and field events, Shanghai's Fu Baolu broke his own national record in the men's pole vault with an exceptional performance of 3.9 meters. The next five athletes also performed extremely well, making it the best harvest of the Games in five days. In the women's javelin throw, Henan's Yuan Hengrui also broke the national record, but it was not as good as ideal. There is no doubt that the three track and field championships for men and women have been firmly secured by Shanghai. The men's and women's track and field events will end today, and the all-around and swimming events will begin tomorrow. The situation in the ball games is becoming increasingly tense, and most have reached the semi-finals, which will be a time of close combat.

Most Fruitful Harvest in Athletics: Fu Bao-Lu's Triumphant Masterpiece; 3.90 Meters Breaks National Record; Runner-Up Wang He Achieves 3.85 Meters, Also Equaling Fu Bao-Lu's National Record

Since the opening of the Games, all athletic events have been completed, but none were truly satisfying. Only yesterday's pole vault can be considered the most fruitful harvest of the Games. The champion was still Fu Bao-Lu, the champion of the fourth and fifth editions, with a result of 3.90 meters, approaching the Far Eastern record. The second-place finisher, Wang He, also reached 3.85 meters, equaling the national record. The results of the third, fourth, fifth, and sixth places were also extremely excellent, all exceeding our expectations. The details of the final competition are recorded below:

Abundant Talent Exceeds Expectations

The competition started at 1:00 PM yesterday and concluded at 6:00 PM. A total of 20 people cleared 3 meters. When the bar was raised to 3.30 meters, 10 people cleared it, including Wu Jing-Shun and Ma Si-Guang from Guangdong; Wang He, Fu Bao-Lu, and Wei Zhi-Ping from Shanghai; Huang Bo-Gang from Jiangxi; Zhang Yu-Chang from Liaoning; Xu Ran-Pan and Chen Yi-Jing from Malaya; and Cai Zi-Xian from Fujian. When the bar was raised to 3.45 meters, Zhang, Huang, Chen, and Cai all failed to clear it, while the others cleared it. When the bar was raised to 3.55 meters, Fu Bao-Lu, Wang He, Ma De-Guang, and Huang Bo-Gang all cleared it, but Wei Zhi-Ping and Wu Jing-Shun failed to clear it. Wei and Wu then jumped again to determine fifth and sixth place, with Wei winning fifth and Wu getting sixth.

Fu and Wang Compete, Performance is Splendid

Then the bar was raised to 3.75 meters. Wang He cleared it with one jump, and Fu Bao-Lu responded in kind, also clearing it with one jump. Ma De-Guang and Huang Bo-Gang failed to clear it. Thus, the two men repeatedly raised and lowered the bar to determine the order. In the end, Huang lost to Ma and got fourth place, while Ma, with the same result, ranked third. Note that Huang Bo-Gang is Huang Yi. He won fourth place in the pole vault at the previous Games. When the bar was raised to 3.85 meters, Fu Bao-Lu cleared it with one jump, and Wang He cleared it with two jumps. The whole stadium erupted in applause, knowing that the national record was sure to be broken. When the bar was raised to 3.90 meters, Wang He jumped first but failed to clear it. Fu also failed to clear it. Then Wang He tried two more jumps but failed, so he was eliminated. Although Fu's great enemy had left, he only had one more chance. At this time, the veteran athlete Feng Jian-Wei was on the field, giving Fu Bao-Lu a massage. After Fu warmed up on the field, his spirits suddenly lifted. He lightly cleared 3.90 meters.

Pole Vault First Place Fu Bao-Lu (Photo by Ye Chang-Lie)

Attempting to Break the Far Eastern Record, Failing by a Hair's Breadth

After that, the referees raised the height of the bar to 4.01 meters. The Far Eastern record is 4.00 meters exactly, and the result of the 10th Far Eastern Games was 3.905 meters. If Mr. Fu could clear 4.01 meters, then the Far Eastern record would be broken. When Fu attempted to jump 4.01 meters, he was able to clear it three times, but unfortunately, his hand made a slight contact with the bar, causing it to fall. Thus, this long-cherished wish was not fulfilled.

Average Results are Wonderful and Impressive

Fu's victory over Wang yesterday was partly due to his strategy. Before the competition, Fu announced that he would not participate and claimed that he had not practiced for two months, cleverly deceiving Wang He. Wang thought he was triumphant but did not expect Fu to achieve this result, leading to his defeat due to underestimating his opponent. The full results are listed below:

The women's javelin event, where Shanghai's Pan Ying-Chu and Qian Hang-Su usually score above 32 meters, was won yesterday by Miss Yuan Heng-Rui from Henan. In the last throw, Ms. Yuan surpassed her even more with 28 and a half meters, leaping to the championship. The other results also improved, and the order also changed. It ended at 2:30 PM, and Zhang Bo-Ling presented the awards. The results are as follows:

Today's Finals Predictions: 10,000 Meters Highly Watchable; National Masters Recalculate Old Scores; Shanxi's Four Generals Worth Attention

Today's 10,000-meter final is sure to be a grand occasion. The participants include Gu De-Sheng, Chen Shu-Sen, and Li Deng-Gui from Shanxi; Niu Hong-Quan and Li Hui from Shandong; Wang Zheng-Lin, Zhang Liang, Jin Kang, and He Bao-Shan from Shanghai. Recalling two years ago, at the Fifth Games held in Nanjing, the 10,000-meter final caused a negotiation issue, and Gu De-Sheng and Jin Jian-Kang became famous. This year, Shanxi has a complete team, and Jiangsu's Jin Zhong-Kang is still healthy. Many of the participants also attended the previous Games. Recalculating old scores is quite intriguing.

Li and Qian Hopeful in Women's 200 Meters

Today's women's 200-meter final will include Li Sen, Qian Hang-Su, Jiao Yu-Lian, Wu Xin-Ju, Tang Qi-Zhen, Deng Yin-Jiao, Chen Keng, Xu Mei-Ying, and Wan Yu-Lian. In the 100 meters, she only ranked fifth. Jiao has also performed well in the 200 meters in the past at the North China Games. Since coming to Shanghai to study at the East Asia Sports College, her results have deteriorated. It is hoped that she will work harder in the future.

Wang Shi-Lin Ill for Triple Jump

Wang Shi-Lin from Beiping is ill and unable to participate in the high jump and long jump. Zhang Jia from Shanghai is more reliable in this event, with a strength of nearly 14 meters. In the Shanghai National Games, he jumped 13.90 meters. Yang Dao-Gui from Nanjing jumped 14.15 meters at the Qingdao summer training camp, and Wang Sen's result at the Beiping Spring Games was 14.18 meters. If Wang participates today, he may still be able to secure a spot; otherwise, the triple jump will be a stage for the competition between Yang and Zhang.

Everyone Says They Are Tired in the 400 Meters

The men's 400-meter final was predicted to produce a national record before the competition because the results of Dong Shu-Zhao, Dai Shu-Guo, and Fu Jin-Cheng are all very impressive. The correspondent met the athletes participating in the 400 meters yesterday and asked for their opinions. They all said they were exhausted and unlikely to achieve good results. Dong Shu-Zhao's participation yesterday was indeed forced because he exerted a lot of effort in the 800-meter competition with Li Shi-Ming the day before, and Li also withdrew from the 400 meters. Fu Jin-Cheng has participated in the finals, repechages, semi-finals, and preliminaries of the 100, 200, and 400 meters, a total of ten times. Dai Shu-Guo has also participated in the finals, semi-finals, repechages, and preliminaries of the 200 and 400 meters. Considering the fatigue levels of the athletes, breaking the national record is likely as difficult as reaching the sky.

New Record in Women's Softball Throw

The national record for women's softball throw will definitely be shattered. The Games record and national record of 45.35 meters will be exceeded by all of the top six. Shanghai's Liang Yun-Sen's result is over 51 meters. Others such as Yuan Heng-Rui from Henan, Yan Xiu-Rong from Guangdong, and Chen Rong-Tang from Shanghai all have results above 45 meters.

Shanghai Has No Problem in Women's Relay

In the women's relay race, the Shanghai team, with Li Sen, Qian Hang-Su, Jiao Yu-Lian, Peng Ai-Pu, and a Westerner participating, is unstoppable. Winning the championship is no problem. Second place will be the Malayan team, and third place will be the Guangdong team. Beiping, Qingdao, Fujian, and Jiangsu will compete for fourth, fifth, and sixth places.

Protests from the Sichuan Team Regarding Doubts in the Pingchuan Soccer Game; Protest Withdrawn After Explanation; No Rest During Extra Time; National Arts Records Verified and Signed This Morning

Yesterday morning's Pingchuan soccer game saw Beijing defeat Sichuan 4-3. The situation was very even and tense. At the end of regulation, the score was tied 2-2. During the 30-minute overtime, the Beijing team scored two goals, while Sichuan only managed to score one. As a result, Beijing eliminated Sichuan with a score of 4-3. After the game, the Sichuan team's leader and coaches protested to the judging committee, claiming that the referee, Lü Changfu, had only counted 27 minutes of the 30-minute overtime, shorting them three minutes, which would have given Sichuan a greater chance to tie the game. The judging committee held a meeting at the gymnasium last night to discuss the Sichuan team's protest. Eleven judges were present, as well as the soccer referee Lü Changfu, two linesmen, and the Sichuan team leader Liu Mianzhi. Regarding the Sichuan team's points, after the referee's explanation, Mr. Liu from the Sichuan team had no objections. Later, Wang Zhengting proposed and Zhang Boling seconded a motion to return the protest letter and deposit to the Sichuan team, as the Sichuan team's protest was actually a request for an explanation from the organizing committee, which was commendable. Thus, the protest ended peacefully. The details are as follows:

Sichuan Team's Protest Content The Sichuan team leader's protest letter was divided into two parts: soccer, and national arts and archery. Each part was further divided into two points. Regarding soccer: (1) The Sichuan team stated that when the game was about to end, with the score tied 2-2, the referee suddenly blew the whistle to stop the game while the Sichuan team was attacking, causing them to lose a scoring opportunity. (2) In the 30-minute overtime, only 27 minutes were played. Although the score was 4-3, the Beijing team was exhausted, and the Sichuan team had a great chance to tie the game. Regarding national arts, they stated that there were errors in the referee's records and requested an explanation.

Soccer Referee's Explanation During the meeting, after the Sichuan team leader presented their case, the chairman, Chen Boling, asked the soccer referee Lü Changfu to respond. Mr. Lü's explanation was as follows: (1) Regarding the unexplained whistle to stop the game, the Sichuan team did not specify which instance they were referring to. In the final minute, the whistle was blown several times. Therefore, this point could not be answered. Based on the facts, the referee would not have blown the whistle without a valid reason. (2) Regarding the three-minute shortage in overtime, Lü explained that according to the rules, there is a 15-minute break between the two 10-minute halves of overtime, and the game is to continue. There is no rest in between. The Sichuan players took a brief rest outside the line at -5 minutes, so the Sichuan team's timing may have mistakenly deducted this rest time. Regarding the national arts portion, it was decided that Chairman Zhang Boling would review the records this morning and provide an answer, which was not expected to be a problem.

Result: Protest Withdrawn After this explanation, Mr. Liu from the Sichuan team stated that the Sichuan team's participation in the Games was not for the sake of winning or losing, but to observe and learn. The protest was merely to draw the organizing committee's attention to and explain the doubts that arose during the game. Therefore, they did not insist on it. Committee member Wang Zhengting then stated that, based on Mr. Liu's previous statements, the entire purpose was to support the Games, not to protest. Now that the explanation was clear, he proposed returning the deposit. Zhang Boling seconded the motion, and the protest letter was returned as well. The meeting adjourned with satisfaction.

Sichuan's Two Protest Letters The Sichuan team leader stated that because the province's soccer team's game against the Beijing soccer team on the morning of the 14th (yesterday) had an unfulfilled overtime and the referee announced the result, they had submitted two protest letters to the organizing committee's judging committee for a public decision. The two protest letters from the team are recorded below:

(1) To the esteemed organizing committee: Today (the 14th), in the morning, the result of our team's soccer game against the Beijing soccer team, according to the organizing committee's report, was 4-3 in favor of Beijing. Our team has two doubts about this game, which are specifically listed on the left: (1) In the second half, when the score was tied 2-2, our team passed the ball into the Beijing team's penalty area, where the defense was very weak, which was very advantageous for our team. There were no fouls or other violations. The referee suddenly blew the whistle to stop the game, giving the Beijing team a good opportunity to wait for reinforcements. The referee then announced the continuation of the game, which greatly affected our team. We request the organizing committee's response. (2) At the end of the second half, the result was 2-2. According to the regulations, there should be a 30-minute overtime. During the overtime, the Beijing team scored two goals, and our team scored one goal, making the score 4-3. In the second half of the overtime, with only 12 minutes elapsed, our team was working hard in the Beijing area and was in a very advantageous position when the referee blew the whistle to announce the end. According to our team leader Liu Shenzhi, who was west of the command platform, soccer coach Deng Deguang, who was at the entrance to the east command platform, and manager Chang Huangxixia, who was in the stands, all timed it and stated that only 12 minutes had elapsed. At that time, our team leader Liu Shenzhi and coach Deng Deguang made verbal protests to the referee, who said that we could report it directly to the organizing committee. We are now submitting the above two reasons, in accordance with Article 21 of the competition regulations, and paying a deposit of ten yuan to the organizing committee within one hour to lodge a protest. We respectfully request a public decision. Addressed to the judging committee.

(2) To the esteemed organizing committee: Our team's archery athlete Liu Yongxi participated in the long-distance archery competition at 1:00 PM today. After the finals, Liu Yongxi's score was 105.05 meters. The referee recorded it as sixth place. Later, due to a proposal from the Henan team leader, a certain athlete's score in the preliminary round was 105.47 meters, but in the finals, it was more than ten meters less than Liu Yongxi's score (Liu Yongxi once had a record of 108.3 meters). The Henan team leader insisted on using the preliminary round score instead of the finals score, so the certain athlete was ranked sixth, and our team's Liu Yongxi was canceled. At that time, our team's athlete Liu Yongxi made a verbal protest to the referee, Mr. Zhang Weizhong, who reported it to the head of the national defense referees, Mr. Chu Minyi. Mr. Chu's response was not very satisfactory and was disappointing. We are now submitting this written protest and respectfully request the organizing committee to make a decision. Addressed to the judging committee.

Soccer

Hong Kong Crushes Anhui 19-0; Beijing Barely Defeats Sichuan 4-3 in Overtime

Yesterday, there were two soccer games. At 9:00 AM, Beijing played Sichuan, with evenly matched strengths, resulting in a fierce battle and a 2-2 tie. After a 30-minute overtime, Beijing narrowly won with a score of 4-3. At 4:00 PM, Hong Kong played Anhui. The Hong Kong team, led by soccer king Li Huitang, was extremely strong and defeated the Anhui team 19-0. This is the victory record of this year's Games' soccer tournament.

Beijing Defeats Sichuan; Wins by One Goal in Overtime

Yesterday morning at 9:00, the soccer game between Beijing and Sichuan saw equally matched teams engage in intense close combat. In the first half, the Sichuan team faced a headwind, making the ball difficult to control. After a long and hard-fought battle, neither side could gain the upper hand. After half an hour, the Beijing team's offense gradually weakened, and Sichuan's center-back Shi Zhaode seized the opportunity to advance, passing the ball to right-winger Zhou Tailin. The inside defenders were unable to intercept, and Zhou kicked the ball into the net. The Beijing team launched a full-line counterattack, but after a long melee, they achieved nothing. Sichuan won the first half with one goal.

In the second half, the teams switched sides, and the Sichuan team had the upper hand, with the momentum in their favor. The Beijing team was cautious and defended tightly. After about twenty minutes of close combat, neither side scored. Before long, the Beijing right-winger dribbled the ball and advanced, breaking through the defenders and passing the ball to the center in front of the goal. Center-forward Lian Qiexun rushed up and kicked the ball, making the score 1-1. The score was evened. Soon, the Sichuan team scored another goal. In the last few minutes, the Beijing center-back desperately broke through the enemy's camp, scoring a valuable point and making the score 2-2 again. The second half suddenly ended.

The referee announced a 30-minute overtime. Only a few minutes after the restart, the Sichuan team lost two goals in a row. The teams switched fields again after 15 minutes, and the Sichuan team worked hard to counterattack. In the last five minutes, right-winger Zhou Tailin scored a goal. The game ended with the sound of the whistle. The total score was 4-3, with victory belonging to Beijing.

Beijing Team

Xu Dumin, Chang Rongzeng, Lü Hongdong, Lin Jixian, Li Zongyu, Huang Pinchang, Xu Peimin, Zhong Guanming, Lian Xuan, Li Hongzong, Wang Dalun

Sichuan Team

Li Pingxi, Lü Su, Chen Changrong, Liu Guoquan, Shi Zhaode, He Rongzhong, Yun Chongqing, Zhou Tailin, Zeng Zhengqi, Ma Zuyin (up), Ouyang Yuan (down), Huang Weixiao

Hong Kong Sweeps Anhui; Sets New Record of 19-0

Yesterday at 4:00 PM, Hong Kong played Anhui. The Hong Kong team was the strongest team in this year's soccer tournament. The forward line was led by soccer king Li Huitang, with left and right wingers Zheng Jiliang and Cao Guicheng charging into battle. Bao Jiaping guarded the goal. They could attack and defend with the best lineup to face the inexperienced Anhui team. They defeated the Anhui team 19-0, setting a new record for goals scored in this year's tournament. The Hong Kong team played with a very relaxed style, and the quality of their play was excellent. Soccer king Li Huitang's footwork and shooting posture were truly captivating and inspiring for the audience. It was especially commendable that he scored eight goals independently. The battle conditions between the two armies are as follows:

The Might of the Soccer King After the kickoff, the soccer king led the army to attack. The disparity in strength between Hong Kong and Anhui made it difficult to resist. The Hong Kong team's three forwards shot many times, hitting the goalposts or being blocked by the goalkeeper at least four or five times. Ten minutes later, the soccer king scored two goals in quick succession. Zhuo Shijin led the uprising and continued to contribute. Zheng Jiliang launched an attack from the wing, scoring another goal. After a brief melee, the soccer king displayed his magical skills again, playing with the Anhui defense as if it were in the palm of his hand, scoring two goals lightly within the defender's area. Shen Tingkun could only watch helplessly as the ball entered the net. Before long, Li Zhaorong sneaked into the Anhui army's restricted area and scored another goal. The Hong Kong team played effortlessly, taking a 7-0 lead. Later, although they had a penalty kick, the soccer king lightly tapped the ball, allowing Shen Tingkun to catch it with ease. The first half ended happily.

Another Beatdown After the break, the teams engaged in close combat. Li Zhaorong continued to intimidate the Anhui team. Li Guowei, although serving as a midfielder, also sent a goal from afar. Zheng Jiliang made another great contribution, and the ball seemed to come to life, also scoring a goal. Before long, Li Zhaorong and Huang Meishun scored again, hitting the mark. The soccer king became excited and scored again. Zhuo Shijin and Huang Meishun followed. The speed of scoring goals was unmatched. Five minutes before the end of the game, the soccer king scored another goal. The score in the second half was 12-0, making the total score 19-0. The Hong Kong team won a great victory. The lineups are as follows:

Hong Kong Team

Soccer Championship Situation

Men's Tennis

Men's Doubles Advances to the Quarterfinals; Shanghai, Malaysia, Java, and Sichuan Advance to the Quarterfinals; Yesterday, Shanghai Barely Defeats Guangdong 3-2

Yesterday, the men's tennis doubles semifinals were held. According to the rules, the best of five sets would determine the winner. Good players from Java, Malaysia, Shanghai, and other places attended. The main event was the match between Shanghai and Guangdong. Initially, the audience was concentrated on the Xu Chengji brothers' match against Hebei, but because it was one-sided, there was little interest. Soon, everyone gathered to watch the Shanghai-Guangdong match. Shanghai fielded Lin Qiu, the strongest doubles combination. However, Xu Runpei and Li Guangjun from Guangdong had excellent cooperation, and their net play and overheads were excellent, posing a significant threat to Lin Qiu. After a fierce five-set battle, the winner was decided. The performance was exceptionally brilliant and rare. In the end, Shanghai, Java, Sichuan, and Malaysia secured the right to advance to the quarterfinals. The results are as follows:

Shanghai-Guangdong Fierce Battle Process Unfavorable Start

Lin Qiu were clumsy and got off to an unfavorable start, falling behind 2-4. Seeing that the situation was not good, they quickly caught up. Lin won his serve, while Li Guangjun made three double faults to give the guests points, tying the score at 4-4. However, after that, Lin Qiu repeatedly made mistakes at critical moments in a winnable situation. In the next game, they won three points in a row, but then lost five points in a row, losing the game. A winnable game turned into a loss, and the situation changed drastically. Xu Li continued to win his serve, taking the lead 6-4.

Wonderful Performance

In the second set, Lin Qiu fought back and played even better, especially as Qiu Youhai gradually got into top form. As a result, they used a two-pronged approach, creating a strong momentum. Li Guangjun and Xu Runpei ran and returned the ball, unwilling to show weakness, competing fiercely. The performance became even more exciting, winning continuous applause. At 2-2 and 3-3, Lin Qiu showed their teamwork and dealt with the situation with all their strength, winning two games in a row, taking a 5-3 lead. The two sides fought for victory in terms of skill and intelligence, which was truly miraculous. Lin then won his serve, winning 6-3.

Winning Two Sets in a Row

In the next set, both sides maintained a strong attacking interest, which was still very strong. Lin Qiu's cooperation was skillful and their net play was incredibly skillful, but their opponents were not afraid to run. They could return balls over the net that others thought were hopeless. Lin Qiu did not relax at all, attacking from both sides and quickly getting four games. In the following few games, Guangdong won two games, but eventually lost again 2-6. Shanghai led 2-1.

Evening Out the Odds

After a break, Guangdong won two games in a row, showing an upward trend. Lin Qiu was unwilling to give in and immediately returned two games. In the fourth game, Qiu Youhai returned a ball from the baseline, hitting the head of a ball boy standing by the net post. The referee immediately ruled that Shanghai lost a point. Lin Qiu both believed that this ball, if it had passed, would have been a good ball. At the same time, Li Guangjun of Guangdong immediately argued that even if this ball had passed the net, it would have been out of bounds. The referee could not make a decision for a while, but after reviewing the line, he still ruled it a good ball. After 3-3, Lin Qiu failed again in depression, losing 3-6. The victory or defeat had to be resolved in the fifth set.

Shanghai-Guangdong Tennis Singles Match: Lin Baohua (right), Xu Runpei (left)

Final Victory

At the beginning of the final, Li Xu's lineup was chaotic, and they repeatedly made mistakes by giving way to each other. Lin Qiu was determined to win, and he would not relax a step. The time was connected to the third level, taking a distant lead. After that, in a lifeless state, they went from 4-1 to 4-2, and then to 5-2. Li Xu attempted a final struggle, and the audience suddenly cheered up, but the tide could not be turned, and Shanghai won the final victory 6-3.

Sichuan Eliminates Nanjing

The Sichuan-Nanjing game lacked energy. Ma Shaobo and Liang Deguang from Nanjing were as quiet as virgins and lacked offensive spirit. They were calm and composed, and Wang Wenzheng and Qian Yaobin could not easily win. In the third set, Nanjing managed to win a set. In the fourth set, both sides attacked with soft balls, which was difficult to resolve. The situation was very even. As a result, Sichuan eliminated Nanjing 3-1.

Java Takes It All

The strength disparity between Xu Chengji and Xu Chengwei of Java and Zheng Bogu and Li Dinggu of Hebei was obvious. The Xu brothers did not demand too much, and easily won 6-2. There was a fierce competition in the second set. Xu won three games first, and Zheng Li tried hard to counterattack, making it 4-3 and then 5-4. Xu then won again 6-4. In the third set, the situation became worse and worse. Zheng Li only won one game. Straight sets, Java eliminated Hebei.

Malaysia Has Great Strength

The Beijing Zaixiao Chao Luo Xiaojian brothers' doubles team once claimed that they hoped to win the National Games championship. Their words were still youthful, but their performance yesterday was indeed impressive. Unfortunately, they encountered Ma Biling Wang Su Ruan Guoying, and under strong pressure, they had no chance to survive, losing three sets in a row. Lin Ruan's doubles team had a tight combination and was a strong enemy of Shanghai. Next week in the quarterfinals, they will meet on a narrow road. It is unknown who will win.

Men's Doubles Situation

Men's Singles Competition: Second Round Concludes Today, Yesterday's Four Matches, Four More Today

Men's tennis has entered a tense phase. The third week of singles matches saw four matches yesterday, and all will conclude today. Those who have already secured a spot in the semi-quarterfinals are Shanghai's Lin Baohua, Qiu Feihai, and Chuan Wang Wenzheng, Qian Yaobin. They will compete tomorrow with today's winners for a place in the quarterfinals. The tennis courtside is expected to be packed with people, becoming extremely crowded.

Yesterday's four singles matches began at 1 p.m. The matches in each group were extremely exciting, drawing a large audience. Veterans Lin and Qiu displayed their prowess, undiminished from their past, while rising stars Xu and Li also showed exceptional talent. Wang Wenzheng's skills are improving daily; he is among the best players. His forehand shot is like a thunderbolt. Even Xu Ji would pale in comparison. The remaining players are all second-tier, possessing considerable skill, and with time, they can certainly be developed. Yesterday's results saw a complete victory for Shanghai, with the scores as follows:

Lin Baohua

The match between Lin and Xu opened the day. Although Xu Runpei was prepared to lose, his spirited resistance was commendable. Lin Baohua was confident and composed. From the start, Lin Baohua shone brightly, launching a fierce attack on young Xu, winning five consecutive games. Xu fought back desperately, winning two games, but it was a fleeting moment of glory. Lin won the next game, ending the first set 6-2. From the second set onward, Lin, riding the momentum of his victory, was in full form. His shots and net play were nearly flawless. Xu tried his best to cope, but to no avail. Lin took a commanding lead of 3-0. Xu then changed his strategy, attacking the net, which proved immediately successful, winning a game. However, it was a pyrrhic victory. Lin feinted and changed his position, sometimes far, sometimes near, leaving Xu exhausted and forced to concede defeat. Lin won the set 6-1.

Xu Chengji's serving posture (Photos by International and Wang Kai)

Qiu Feihai

Qiu Feihai is aging and his skills are declining, but with long experience on the court, he remains seasoned. Li Guangjun, a Guangdong athlete, is excellent at smashing and cutting, but his temper is too quick, and he lacks patience. At the start of the match, Li, facing a strong opponent, was unusually flustered, hitting weak shots and lacking control. Qiu attacked with full force, relentlessly, hitting long shots deep into both corners, and had an easy time, winning six consecutive games. When the second set began, Qiu was already exhausted, while Li gradually regained his composure, determined to take revenge. As a result, the situation became even, and the competition was fierce. They tied at one game each, then two games each. Li Guangjun also showed signs of fatigue, and the two players battled back and forth. The players were completely drained by the match. At 4-2, then 5-4, Li led twice, but ultimately, due to lack of experience, he lost his temper and made numerous unforced errors. As a result, Qiu added three more games, sealing the victory at 7-5.

Wang Wenzheng

Wang Wenzheng is highly skilled but arrogant, and repeatedly underestimates his opponents. He almost lost to Ma Shaobo of Nanjing yesterday, suffering from the same problem. After the start, Ma fought bravely and successfully, taking a 2-0 lead. Later, he employed several sweeping shots, turning defeat into victory, winning the first set 6-2. Wang found it difficult to change his nature. The old problem resurfaced, and he became arrogant and dismissive, thinking his opponent's skills were average and not worth considering. Unexpectedly, the player from Nanjing was exceptionally strong, winning four consecutive games, threatening to break through completely. The spectators were stunned, and Wenzheng himself was shocked, realizing his opponent was not to be underestimated. He quickly focused and fought carefully. As expected, his skills were superior, and he made several successful plays, quickly gaining momentum, winning six consecutive games and winning the second set 6-4.

The Wei sisters, who have won the right to the women's doubles quarterfinals (Photo by Ye Changlie)

Qian Yaobin

Where there are no great generals in Shu, Liao Hua acts as the vanguard. At the previous National Games, Lin Baohua took the stage as a general, with Qian Yaobin as his vanguard. This time, Wang Wenzheng is filling in, while the vanguard position remains with Qian. After a two-year absence, Qian's skills remain the same, without any improvement. Li Buzu of Nanjing, a renowned player from the capital, possesses considerable strength. Comparing the two, they are evenly matched. The ultimate victory yesterday went to Qian, due to his superior stamina. In the first set, Li attacked aggressively, winning 6-4. Qian was unwilling to give in, and in the second set, he fought back bravely, hitting shots to the left and right, returning the favor, winning with the same score of 6-4. The third set was a battle for survival, and the competition was even fiercer. However, Li had expended too much energy in the first two sets, and his stamina gradually declined. Qian maintained his strength, attacking relentlessly. Li only managed to win one game and was eliminated with a score of 6-1.

Men's Basketball

Beijing Easily Defeats Henan; Qingdao Struggles to Eliminate Malayan Chinese; Philippine Islands Win Big Over Sichuan; Nanjing Ousts Shandong; No Matches on the Men's Basketball Western Front Today

Yesterday's basketball games at the gymnasium were delayed until after 9 a.m. due to a memorial week event held in the gymnasium at 8 a.m. The first match was between Beijing and Henan. Beijing's strength was far superior, and Henan was no match for them. The Qingdao vs. Malayan Chinese game was fiercely contested. In the end, Malayan Chinese lost by a narrow margin of eight points. Philippine Islands won big over Sichuan with a score of 100 to 22. Nanjing vs. Shandong saw Nanjing field a non-standard lineup in the first half, allowing Shandong to hold their own. In the second half, Nanjing's best five players took to the court, and Shandong faltered, ultimately losing by 68 to 36 and being eliminated. Today will be entirely dedicated to the second round of women's basketball. On the men's side, the western front is quiet, with no matches scheduled. Yesterday's competition results:

The first-round match between Beijing and Henan was held yesterday at 9:30 a.m. Beijing has many veteran players with a wealth of experience. Initially, they did not play at full strength, so the situation did not become tense. Later, Mu Zuoyun and Yu Jingxiao showed their skills, and Henan's defense was ravaged. The team's cooperation and techniques were quite good, but their movements seemed slightly slow, likely because they had not met a worthy opponent. At the start of the match, Li Baoshan of Beijing committed a foul during a passing sequence. Li Enlong of Henan scored the first point. Li Guochong of Beijing launched a swift attack, scoring several consecutive points. Yu Jingxiao had been lying in wait, scoring two goals. Although the Henan army tried to fight back, Beijing's defense was impregnable. They only managed to score a few points with long shots. In the second half, the Beijing team became increasingly dominant, and Henan was unable to keep up. Yao Yelian and Li Enlong were also subsequently penalized and left the court, leading to an irreversible situation. As a result, they were soundly defeated by 74 to 30.

Men's Basketball Situation

Men's Baseball

Shanghai Eliminates Hebei; To Compete with Guangdong for Championship on the 18th; Yesterday's Score: 9 to 2 Against Hebei

The Shanghai baseball team defeated Hebei yesterday in the semi-final (Group B) with a score of 9 to 2, securing the right to compete in the final. They are scheduled to vie for the championship against Guangdong, the defending champions, on the 18th. The upcoming duel between these two powerhouses is highly anticipated. Yesterday, Shanghai's pitcher, Gan Zhen, demonstrated remarkable skill, allowing only two hits in nine innings, which was no easy feat. Reliever He Xiancheng, with his seasoned experience and thoughtful approach, collaborated with the entire team to achieve victory. Hebei's pitchers, Zhang Minhui and reliever Gong Qingzong, were far less skilled than their Shanghai counterparts, displaying weaknesses. However, the infield and outfield coordination was adequate, preventing major errors despite the adverse circumstances. The ball umpire was Zhang Guodong, the base umpire was Chen Futian, and the recorder was Li Baojun.

Battle Lines Drawn, Shanghai Takes the Lead

Hebei took the field to attack first, while Shanghai waited in readiness. Bao Nvpei was first up but was caught out in center field. Chen Bingchou followed, safely reaching first base. He attempted to steal second but was injured and replaced by Bao Wenpei. Then Zhang Minhui hit a double, and Bao, amidst applause, ran back to the base, fulfilling his important mission. However, Zhang's ambitions were thwarted by the subsequent batters' lack of success. When Shanghai switched to offense, Zhou Jun hit and reached first base. The Guangdong pitcher threw a wild pitch, allowing Zhou to advance to second. Liang Chengson then hit, and Zhou returned home victorious. When Zeng Ruiqi hit, Hebei's defense was thrown into disarray, allowing Liang Chengson to score easily. In the first inning, Shanghai took the lead with a score of 2 to 1. In the second inning, none of Hebei's three batters survived. Shanghai engaged in aggressive play, with An Lesheng starting with a double. Fang Guanshao followed and advanced. He Xiancheng lightly tapped, and An Lesheng scored. Zhou Jun and Liang Chengson joined the fray, and second base was full of Shanghai players. Zeng Ruiqi made a hit, and Zhou returned. In the second inning, Shanghai scored two points, while Hebei scored zero.

Soldiers Fighting, Heaven and Earth Change Color

The third inning passed uneventfully. The fourth inning saw a fierce battle. After Hebei lost momentum, Shanghai seized the opportunity and advanced. He Xiancheng scored the first point. Within five minutes, Shanghai's players filled all three bases. Zeng Ruiqi hit a double, and Zhou Jun and Liang Chengson returned home in succession. Liang Fuchu, known as a lucky general, hit a ball that sent Zeng back to base. In this inning, Shanghai scored four points, securing the victory. In the fifth inning, Fang Guanshao performed another miracle, his return to base due to a wild pitch by Hebei's pitcher. The sixth inning saw only minor contact between the two sides, with no gains or losses. In the seventh inning, the entire Hebei team made a concerted effort to attack, and Gong Qingzong, through repeated efforts, finally scored a point. The subsequent players were also strong and capable. All three bases saw Hebei players. Unfortunately, they were repeatedly caught out, wasting all their efforts. In this inning, Hebei scored one point, while Shanghai scored zero. The eighth and ninth innings returned to a quiet state. Hebei gained nothing, and Shanghai abandoned the ninth inning. The final score was Shanghai 9, Hebei 2.

Women's Softball

Previous Women's Softball Champion Guangdong Loses to Shandong; Seven Innings Result in 7 to 2; Shanghai vs. Hebei Today

The women's softball semi-final (Group A) between Shandong and Guangdong took place yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM. Shandong excelled on average and defeated Guangdong with a score of 7 to 2, securing the right to compete in the final. The ball umpire was Shen Guoquan, the base umpire was Gao Zi, and the recorder was Xia Kaiming. Today at 2:00 PM, Shanghai will face Hebei, who lost to Jiangsu, in the semi-final (Group B). The winning team will compete against Shandong for the championship on the afternoon of the 17th at 2:00 PM. The future battle is imminent.

Zhang Muxia Establishes Immortal Merit

Shandong's victory was largely due to pitcher Zhang Muxia. Apart from allowing four hits to the opponent in the second and third innings, she and the infield and outfield adopted a containment strategy in the remaining five innings, leaving the enemy astonished and unable to advance. On the attacking side, she hit a home run in both the first and fifth innings, establishing immortal merit and securing victory. Others, such as Wang Fengjie, Jin Zhiban, and Xu Jun, were skilled at hitting. The team's collaboration was quite polished, showing great promise for the championship.

Zhuo Jin-yi, First on Base

Guangdong's performance was still respectable, and their inner and outer lines responded well. Unfortunately, the pitcher's skills were mediocre, sowing the seeds of much trouble. Even more unfortunate was that the team made many mistakes in the first inning, resulting in great losses. In the fifth inning, when the opponent had already taken two outs, the pitcher became careless and suffered another major blow. Not many were skilled at hitting. Zhuo Jin-yi was considered a master in this regard, first hitting a double, becoming the first Guangdong player to return to base. Liang Shiyi also had a hit in the third inning, scoring a point. All others returned empty-handed.

Tense Seven-Inning Battle

Shandong took the field to challenge, with Wang Fengjie first hitting a high ball. Guangdong's shortstop missed the catch, allowing her to advance to first base, then steal second. Jin Zhiban hit a triple, and Wang returned home. Due to Guangdong's mistakes, Jin also took advantage and returned. Xu Jun hit a high ball, which was caught out. Zhang Muxia then hit a home run, greatly boosting the entire team. Subsequently, both players failed to score. In the first inning, Shandong scored three points, while Guangdong failed to counter. At that time, a minor issue arose, causing a dispute, but it was soon resolved, and the match continued as normal. In the second inning, Guangdong's Zhuo Jin-yi hit a double, boosting morale. Lun Gong then hit a triple and later returned to base on a wild pitch. In this inning, Shandong scored zero, while Guangdong scored one. In the third inning, Guangdong scored another point, while Shandong still scored nothing. The score was two to three, with Guangdong showing signs of making a comeback. In the fourth inning, neither side made progress. In the fifth inning, Shandong's Zhang Muxia hit a home run, with four players returning at once, securing the victory. In the following two innings, both sides remained defensive, with no further developments. The result was 7 to 2, with Shandong winning. Shandong's pitcher was Zhang Muxia, with Jin Zhiban as catcher, while Guangdong's pitcher was Liang Shiyi, with Liang Zhuangjian as catcher.

Men's Volleyball

Malayan Wins Against Nanjing Yesterday; Tibet Forfeits, Guangdong Wins Without Effort

The men's volleyball competition concluded yesterday with two matches: Malaya versus Nanjing, and Guangdong versus Tibet. Malaya narrowly defeated Nanjing in a hard-fought battle, while Tibet forfeited the second match, allowing Guangdong to win without effort. The score between Malaya and Nanjing is as follows:

(1) Malaya Wins Against Nanjing

Fengshui Surveyed, Malaya Wins First

At 1:00 PM, Chen Dedao took his place on the platform and surveyed the fengshui. Nanjing launched the first attack, making good progress. However, out of nowhere, Malaya, despite being on the defensive, redoubled its efforts. Liang Juhe served well, with the ball landing on the edge of the opponent's court. Nanjing attempted a save, but the Malayan front-row blockade was impenetrable. Continuous serves caused Nanjing to not only lose ground but also shake its stronghold. In a state of panic, Nanjing fell behind with a score of 6 to 11. Changing formations, they launched an aggressive counterattack, but due to unrealistic expectations, they were unable to salvage the situation, ending the match at 21 to 12.

Back Route Severed, Nanjing Loses Again

At the start of the second game, Malaya, riding the momentum of their initial victory, went on the offensive, scoring three consecutive points. Nanjing returned the favor, adopting the same tactic and scoring three points. This provided a slight turning point for Nanjing. At 8 to 9, Nanjing scored another point, making the score 8 to 10. However, the recorder, in a muddled state, announced Malaya 11, and the referee ordered a change of sides. The Nanjing team and some spectators were confused. After a correction and resumption of the game, Nanjing changed sides with a score of 11 to 10. Subsequently, the Nanjing third-row military was shaken. Despite the will to advance, the back route was severed, and they ultimately lost the second game with a score of 21 to 17.

Occasional Mistakes Lead to Great Errors

Both sides added new forces to the battle in the third game, advancing and retreating, with no significant achievements. The first half of the game passed uneventfully. In the second half, Malaya became more aggressive, with each player showing brilliant performance. However, good times don't last. At a significant difference of 17 to 10, an occasional mistake became a great error. Nanjing advanced step by step, while Malaya retreated steadily. Team captain Zheng Jimin repeatedly issued warnings and instructions, but in the end, Nanjing turned the game around with a difference of two points, 19 to 21.

Wonderful Performance Buries Nanjing

At the start of the fourth game, Nanjing was even more arrogant. Their morale was high, aiming to turn the tide. In the first half, Malaya was lifeless. At the change of sides, the difference was still 11 to 3. It is regrettable that Nanjing, at this crucial juncture, gave up on themselves and easily relaxed, allowing Malaya to level the score in an instant. Seeing their great position threatened, Nanjing rallied their spirits and fought to the death, with mutual concessions and advances. Each side made achievements. Thus, the scores were close, and the competition became fiercer. For a time, the gunfire was deafening, and the bullets rained down, becoming the most exciting scene of the entire game. In the last five minutes, Malaya's Situ obtained the pass from the second-row setter and jumped high to kill the Nanjing life with an absolute technique. The comparison was 25 to 13, and Malaya eliminated Nanjing with a score of three to one.

(2) Guangdong Wins Against Tibet

Tibet Forfeits, Wins Without Effort

The Guangdong-Tibet match was scheduled to start at 3:00 PM. The Guangdong team arrived at the venue at 1:30 PM to practice. By 3:10 PM, the scheduled time had passed, but the Tibet team had not yet arrived. The referee declared the team to have forfeited, and the victory belonged to Guangdong. (3) Yu Declares Forfeiture
